[C21] METALLURGY -- C21 in the Cooperative Patent Classification covers metallurgical processes, including the extraction of metals from ores, refining, alloy production, and treatment of metals and alloys. It also includes methods for shaping, heat-treating, and surface-coating metals, as well as related apparatus and equipment used in these operations.
[C21B] MANUFACTURE OF IRON OR STEEL -- **Definition:** This place covers:
[C21B 11/00] Making pig-iron other than in blast furnaces -- This class deals with processes for producing pig iron by methods other than the conventional blast furnace, including direct reduction, rotary hearth, electric arc or other alternative reduction techniques. It covers the preparation of molten iron from iron ore, scrap or other feedstock using non-blast furnace reactors.
[C21B 11/02] in low shaft furnaces -- The CPC subclass C21B 11/02 deals with the production of pig-iron in low-shaft furnaces such as puddling or reverberatory furnaces as an alternative to blast-furnace methods. It falls under metallurgy and the manufacture of iron or steel, describing processes where the furnace height is relatively small and the charge is melted and tapped in a vertical arrangement.
[C21B 11/06] in rotary kilns -- C21B 11/06 refers to the production of pig iron using rotary kilns, where iron ore and a reductant are heated and reduced as the kiln rotates, providing an alternative to conventional blast-furnace methods. The classification lies within chemistry-based metallurgy for iron and steel manufacturing.
[C21B 11/08] in hearth-type furnaces -- The C21B 11/08 subclass covers the production of pig-iron in hearth-type furnaces, such as open-hearth or reverberatory furnaces, rather than in blast furnaces. It includes methods that melt iron ore and scrap in a hearth, control temperature and composition, and tap the molten pig-iron for further processing.
[C21B 11/10] in electric furnaces -- C21B 11/10 pertains to the production of pig-iron in electric furnaces, describing methods that replace traditional blast-furnace operations within the metallurgy branch of iron and steel manufacturing.
[C21B 13/00] Making spongy iron or liquid steel, by direct processes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Direct reduction processes obtaining either sponge iron or molten iron or steel.  Inventions which concern the treatment of the reducing gases, the solid reductant, the ores, the reduced iron or the addition of fluxes or the treatment of the ores in a fluidised bed or lead to attainment of molten iron or steel.
[C21B 13/0006] obtaining iron or steel in a molten state -- It covers methods for producing molten iron or steel directly from raw materials, typically using reduction of iron ore in a furnace to obtain liquid metal without intermediate solid forms. The classification falls under manufacturing of iron or steel, focusing on spongy iron and liquid steel via direct processes.
[C21B 13/0013] introduction of iron oxide into a bath of molten iron containing a carbon reductant -- The code refers to a step in direct iron-making processes where iron oxide is added to a bath of molten iron that already contains a carbon reductant. This introduction helps control the composition and temperature of the melt during the production of spongy iron or liquid steel.
[C21B 13/002] Reduction of iron ores by passing through a heated column of carbon -- The subclass covers direct-reduction processes where iron ore is passed through a heated column containing carbon, allowing the carbon to act as the reducing agent and produce spongy iron or molten steel. It includes methods that use solid carbon sources such as coke or charcoal and designs like shaft or rotary furnaces.
[C21B 13/0026] introduction of iron oxide in the flame of a burner or a hot gas stream -- C21B 13/0026 relates to the direct production of spongy iron or liquid steel in which iron oxide is fed into the flame of a burner or into a hot gas stream. The introduction of the oxide modifies the reduction or heating reactions within the furnace, aiding control of temperature and composition.
[C21B 13/0033] In fluidised bed furnaces or apparatus containing a dispersion of the material -- The subclass C21B 13/0033 covers the production of spongy iron or liquid steel by direct reduction in fluidised-bed furnaces or other apparatus where the material is dispersed in a fluidised medium. It addresses processes that create a suspension of iron-bearing particles and a reducing gas or liquid to achieve metallurgical reduction. This method is used for efficient, continuous steelmaking in a fluidised environment.
[C21B 13/004] in a continuous way by reduction from ores -- C21B 13/004 covers methods for producing spongy iron or liquid steel in a continuous process by directly reducing metal ores. It falls under the metallurgy branch of chemistry, specifically the manufacture of iron or steel, and addresses direct reduction techniques rather than melting.
[C21B 13/0046] making metallised agglomerates or iron oxide -- This subclass covers processes for producing metallised agglomerates or iron oxide as intermediates in the direct production of spongy iron or liquid steel. It involves agglomerating iron particles with a metallic coating to improve handling or reactivity before further reduction.
[C21B 13/0053] On a massing grate -- C21B 13/0053 covers a massing grate used in the direct production of spongy iron or liquid steel, where molten metal is collected on a perforated platform before being removed from the furnace. The grate enables controlled discharge of the metal while maintaining furnace temperature and slag separation.
[C21B 13/006] Starting from ores containing non ferrous metallic oxides -- This CPC subclass covers processes for producing spongy iron or liquid steel where the feedstock comprises ores that contain non-ferrous metal oxides, such as copper or lead oxides, and these oxides are reduced together with iron oxides in a direct reduction or smelting operation. The method uses the non-ferrous oxides as part of the raw material mix rather than as separate by-products.
[C21B 13/0066] Preliminary conditioning of the solid carbonaceous reductant -- The CPC subclass C21B 13/0066 covers the early treatment of solid carbonaceous reductants before they are used in direct iron or steel making processes. It includes steps such as drying, crushing, screening, sieving, blending or pre-heating of the material to obtain the required size, moisture content or homogeneity for efficient reduction in spongy iron or liquid steel production.
[C21B 13/0073] Selection or treatment of the reducing gases -- The subclass C21B 13/0073 concerns the selection and conditioning of the reducing gases employed in direct-reduction processes that produce spongy iron or liquid steel, including choices of gas composition, temperature, pressure, impurity removal, recycling and other treatments that optimise the reduction reaction.
[C21B 13/008] Use of special additives or fluxing agents -- C21B 13/008 covers the introduction of special additives or fluxing agents during direct processes that produce spongy iron or liquid steel. The classification includes substances that modify slag chemistry, enhance reduction or melting efficiency, aid impurity removal, or otherwise improve the metallurgical performance of the process.
[C21B 13/0086] Conditioning, transformation of reduced iron ores -- The CPC subclass C21B 13/0086 covers processes that condition or transform reduced iron ores during the direct-reduction production of spongy iron or liquid steel. It includes techniques for preparing, agitating, heating, or otherwise treating the reduced ore to improve its properties before final melting or casting. This subclass falls under metallurgy and the manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21B 13/0093] Protecting against oxidation -- This subclass concerns methods or additives used to prevent oxidation of iron or steel during direct production of spongy iron or liquid steel. It includes protective atmospheres, coatings, or alloying elements applied in the melting or solidification stage. The code C21B 13/0093 falls under manufacturing of iron or steel in the CPC.
[C21B 13/02] in shaft furnaces -- C21B 13/02 classifies the production of spongy iron or liquid steel using shaft furnaces, a direct process that reduces iron ore without a separate melting stage. It falls under metallurgy, specifically manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21B 13/023] wherein iron or steel is obtained in a molten state -- The CPC subclass C21B 13/023 covers direct processes that yield iron or steel already in a molten condition, such as liquid steel produced by reduction or smelting without an intermediate solid stage. It falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Manufacture of iron or steel → Making spongy iron or liquid steel, by direct processes.
[C21B 13/026] heated electrically -- C21B 13/026 refers to the direct production of spongy iron or liquid steel using electrical heating. The subclass covers processes where electric energy is applied to melt or reduce iron ore or scrap, producing molten steel without intermediate chemical reduction steps.
[C21B 13/029] Introducing coolant gas in the shaft furnaces -- The subclass C21B 13/029 covers the introduction of a coolant gas into shaft furnaces used for direct processes that produce spongy iron or liquid steel. It includes methods and apparatus for feeding, distributing or controlling inert or cooling gases to regulate furnace temperature, protect the lining and improve the quality of the metallurgical product.
[C21B 13/04] in retorts -- C21B 13/04 covers the direct production of spongy iron or liquid steel using retorts, where the metal is reduced or melted in a sealed vessel under controlled conditions. The process involves heating iron ore or feedstock in the retort to generate the desired molten or porous metal without intermediate steps.
[C21B 13/06] in multi-storied furnaces -- C21B 13/06 covers the production of spongy iron or liquid steel by direct reduction or melting in multi-storied furnace arrangements, where the furnace consists of several horizontal levels stacked vertically to improve heat utilization and material flow.
[C21B 13/08] in rotary furnaces -- The subclass C21B 13/08 covers the production of spongy iron or liquid steel using direct processes that are carried out in rotary furnaces. It pertains to metallurgical methods where the raw material is heated and reduced in a rotating-cylindrical vessel, enabling continuous flow and improved temperature control. This falls under the broader categories of chemistry, metallurgy and manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21B 13/085] wherein iron or steel is obtained in a molten state -- This subclass covers processes for producing spongy iron or liquid steel directly where the metal is obtained in a molten condition. It relates to the metallurgical manufacturing of iron or steel, specifically direct reduction methods that yield a molten product rather than a solid bloom. The CPC code C21B 13/085 captures these molten-state direct processes.
[C21B 13/10] in hearth-type furnaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also rotary-hearth furnaces.
[C21B 13/105] Rotary hearth-type furnaces -- C21B 13/105 covers rotary hearth-type furnaces used in the direct production of spongy iron or liquid steel. These furnaces consist of a rotating hearth that continuously moves molten metal through heating zones for refining and alloying. The classification applies to processes where the metal is melted or treated directly within such rotary equipment.
[C21B 13/12] in electric furnaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also using a plasma.
[C21B 13/125] By using plasma -- The subclass C21B 13/125 covers direct metallurgical processes in which a plasma torch provides the heat and reactive environment for producing spongy iron or liquid steel, eliminating the need for a conventional furnace. It falls under the C21B hierarchy for manufacture of iron or steel using direct reduction or melting methods.
[C21B 13/14] Multi-stage processes -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Inventions in which different types of installations are used in sequence to arrive either at a solid or a molten product.
[C21B 13/143] Injection of partially reduced ore into a molten bath -- C21B 13/143 covers the step in direct iron and steel making where partially reduced ore is injected into a molten bath to complete reduction and produce liquid steel. This technique is used in processes that create spongy iron or melt steel without a separate furnace, improving efficiency and integrating reduction with melting stages.
[C21B 13/146] Multi-step reduction without melting -- C21B 13/146 classifies processes that produce spongy iron or liquid steel through a series of reduction steps that are carried out without melting the material. It covers direct reduction methods where the ore is progressively reduced in solid or semi-solid form, typically in a furnace or reactor, before any final melting step is applied. This subclass is used for technologies such as solid-state reduction, gas-based reduction sequences, and other non-melting chemistries in iron and steel manufacture.
[C21B 15/00] Other processes for the manufacture of iron from iron compounds -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also processes involving nuclear energy or a chloride process.
[C21B 15/003] By using nuclear energy -- C21B 15/003 covers processes for producing iron from iron compounds that employ nuclear energy, such as neutron irradiation or other radiation-induced reduction methods. It is classified under "Other processes for the manufacture of iron from iron compounds" within the metallurgy section of the CPC, addressing innovative, nuclear-based metallurgical techniques.
[C21B 15/006] By a chloride process -- C21B 15/006 covers metallurgical methods that produce iron from iron compounds using a chloride route, where the material is first converted into iron chlorides and then reduced to metallic iron. The classification applies to any process that relies on chlorine-containing reagents for the conversion, falling under other processes for iron manufacture.
[C21B 15/02] Metallothermic processes, e.g. thermit reduction -- C21B 15/02 covers metallothermic processes for producing iron, in which a more reactive metal such as aluminum reduces iron compounds in a highly exothermic reaction, exemplified by the thermite reduction method.
[C21B 15/04] from iron carbonyl -- C21B 15/04 covers processes that produce iron or steel by decomposing iron carbonyl compounds. It includes steps such as thermal decomposition, reduction or precipitation to recover metallic iron from the carbonyl precursor, often for specialized alloy or powder production.
[C21B 2005/005] Selection or treatment of the reducing gases -- C21B 2005/005 covers processes that select, condition, or treat gases employed as reducing agents, including purification, moisture removal, impurity separation, and adjustment of composition or temperature before the gases are introduced into a metallurgical or chemical operation. The subclass applies to any method that prepares the reducing gas to meet specified performance criteria.
[C21B 2100/00] Handling of exhaust gases produced during the manufacture of iron or steel -- C21B 2100/00 covers methods and equipment for treating or disposing of the exhaust gases generated in iron and steel production. It includes scrubbing, filtration, cooling and recycling techniques aimed at reducing pollutants such as dust, carbon monoxide and sulfur compounds.
[C21B 2100/20] Increasing the gas reduction potential of recycled exhaust gases
[C21B 2100/22] by reforming -- The CPC subclass C21B 2100/22 deals with technologies that handle exhaust gases generated in iron and steel production by means of reforming. It includes catalytic or thermal processes that convert harmful gases such as CO, CO₂, NOₓ into less polluting compounds or useful synthesis gas, often to improve environmental performance and recover energy.
[C21B 2100/24] by shift reactions -- C21B 2100/24 covers methods that treat exhaust gases generated in iron-or-steel production by employing shift reactions, typically converting carbon monoxide to carbon dioxide and hydrogen to manage emissions and recover energy. It falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Manufacture of iron or steel, specifically the handling of exhaust gases.
[C21B 2100/26] by adding additional fuel in recirculation pipes -- C21B 2100/26 deals with handling exhaust gases from iron or steel manufacturing by injecting additional fuel into recirculation pipes, a technique that alters combustion conditions to aid energy recovery or reduce pollutant emissions.
[C21B 2100/28] by separation -- C21B 2100/28 covers processes for handling exhaust gases generated in iron and steel production by separating the pollutants from the gas stream. It includes techniques such as filtration, cyclonic separation, electrostatic precipitation and other physical separation methods used to remove dust, particulate matter and gases before release.
[C21B 2100/282] of carbon dioxide
[C21B 2100/284] of nitrogen -- The subclass C21B 2100/284 covers methods and apparatus for handling nitrogen-containing exhaust gases generated in iron or steel production, including techniques for removal, reduction, recirculation or abatement of nitrogen oxides to meet environmental regulations.
[C21B 2100/40] Gas purification of exhaust gases to be recirculated or used in other metallurgical processes -- This subclass covers methods and apparatus for cleaning exhaust gases generated during iron or steel production so that the purified gases can be recirculated within the plant or employed in other metallurgical operations. It includes removal of pollutants such as dust, carbon monoxide, sulfur compounds, and nitrogen oxides before the gases are reused.
[C21B 2100/42] Sulphur removal -- The CPC entry C21B 2100/42 covers any process that removes sulphur compounds from the gases emitted during iron or steel production. It includes methods such as scrubbing, chemical absorption, adsorption or precipitation that treat exhaust streams to reduce sulphur emissions before release.
[C21B 2100/44] Removing particles, e.g. by scrubbing, dedusting
[C21B 2100/60] Process control or energy utilisation in the manufacture of iron or steel -- C21B 2100/60 covers methods and systems for controlling processes or using energy efficiently during iron and steel production, including monitoring, regulation, and recovery of waste heat or exhaust gases. It relates to optimizing operational parameters to improve productivity, reduce emissions, and lower energy consumption in metallurgical processes.
[C21B 2100/62] Energy conversion other than by heat exchange, e.g. by use of exhaust gas in energy production -- The code covers technologies that convert the energy of exhaust gases generated during iron or steel production into usable power without relying on conventional heat-exchange processes. It includes methods such as direct combustion-driven turbines, gas-fuel cells or other systems that harness exhaust-gas energy for electricity or mechanical work.
[C21B 2100/64] Controlling the physical properties of the gas, e.g. pressure or temperature -- C21B 2100/64 relates to methods and apparatus for controlling the physical properties of exhaust gases generated in iron or steel production, such as adjusting pressure, temperature, or flow rate to optimise process performance or reduce emissions. The subclass falls under the chemistry and metallurgy hierarchy, focusing on handling of exhaust gases during metal manufacture.
[C21B 2100/66] Heat exchange -- The CPC subclass C21B 2100/66 covers heat-exchange devices and methods used to treat the exhaust gases generated in iron and steel production. It includes equipment such as recuperators, regenerators and condensers that recover thermal energy from furnace off-gas streams, improving energy efficiency and reducing emissions.
[C21B 2100/80] Interaction of exhaust gases produced during the manufacture of iron or steel with other processes -- This class covers the use or treatment of exhaust gases generated during iron or steel production by linking them to other industrial processes, such as heat recovery, chemical synthesis, or combined-cycle operations, to improve efficiency or reduce emissions.
[C21B 2200/00] Recycling of non-gaseous waste material -- The code C21B 2200/00 covers methods for recovering and reusing solid waste generated during iron or steel production, such as slags, dust, and other non-gaseous residues. It includes physical, chemical or metallurgical processes that convert waste into usable material or reduce its environmental impact.
[C21B 2300/00] Process aspects -- This CPC subclass C21B 2300/00 covers process aspects related to the manufacture of iron or steel within the field of metallurgy. It includes methods, steps and conditions used in producing iron or steel, such as melting, refining, casting and treatment processes.
[C21B 2300/02] Particular sequence of the process steps -- The CPC class C21B 2300/02 falls under chemistry, metallurgy, manufacture of iron or steel and process aspects and defines the protection of inventions that specify a particular sequence of the steps in a steel-making process, such as the order of heating, reduction, alloying or cooling operations.
[C21B 2300/04] Modeling of the process, e.g. for control purposes -- This CPC subclass concerns the development of mathematical or computer models of iron or steel manufacturing processes for control and optimization purposes. It includes simulation, predictive modeling and the formulation of control strategies to improve process performance.
[C21B 2400/00] Treatment of slags originating from iron or steel processes -- This class covers processes that treat slags produced during iron or steel production, including their cooling, granulation, physicochemical conversion, and disposal or recycling to recover valuable components. Techniques may involve leaching, magnetic separation, or thermal treatment to reduce waste and enable material reuse.
[C21B 2400/02] Physical or chemical treatment of slags -- The CPC subclass C21B 2400/02 covers methods for physically or chemically treating slags that arise during the manufacture of iron or steel. It includes processes such as cooling, grinding, leaching, neutralisation or other treatments aimed at stabilising, recovering valuable components or preparing the slag for disposal or reuse. This subclass falls under the chemistry-metallurgy hierarchy for the treatment of slags originating from iron or steel processes.
[C21B 2400/022] Methods of cooling or quenching molten slag -- The CPC entry C21B 2400/022 covers techniques for cooling or quenching molten slag generated in iron or steel production. It details processes that rapidly reduce slag temperature to control solidification, improve handling, and recover valuable components, falling under the broader treatment of metallurgical slags.
[C21B 2400/024] with the direct use of steam or liquid coolants, e.g. water -- The subclass C21B 2400/024 covers processes for treating slags generated in iron or steel production that employ direct cooling with steam, water or other liquid coolants. It includes methods where the coolant is applied to the slag to lower its temperature, improve solidification or facilitate subsequent handling and disposal. This approach is used to enhance safety and efficiency in slag management.
[C21B 2400/026] using air, inert gases or removable conductive bodies -- The C21B 2400/026 subclass covers methods for treating slags generated in iron or steel production by introducing air, inert gases or removable conductive bodies to the molten slag. These techniques aim to modify slag chemistry, temperature or viscosity, facilitating removal, recycling or further processing of the material.
[C21B 2400/028] with the permanent addition of cooled slag or other solids -- C21B 2400/028 covers metallurgical methods that treat slags generated in iron or steel production by permanently incorporating cooled slag or other solid materials into the treatment process, such as adding these solids back into furnaces, ladles or slag-handling streams to modify slag composition, viscosity or cooling behaviour.
[C21B 2400/03] Removing sulfur -- The CPC entry C21B 2400/03, titled Removing sulfur, covers processes used to extract or reduce sulfur present in slags generated during iron or steel production. It includes chemical, physical or thermal treatments designed to lower the sulfur content of the molten or solid slag.
[C21B 2400/032] Separating slag from liquid, e.g. from water, after quenching -- C21B 2400/032 covers processes for separating solid slag from a liquid medium after quenching, such as water, in iron or steel production. It includes methods like sedimentation, filtration, decanting or other mechanical means used to remove slag particles from the liquid phase.
[C21B 2400/034] Stirring or agitating by pressurised fluids or by moving apparatus -- The CPC entry C21B 2400/034 covers methods for stirring or agitating slags generated in iron or steel production by means of pressurised fluids or mechanically moving equipment, facilitating their treatment and processing within metallurgical operations.
[C21B 2400/04] Specific shape of slag after cooling -- C21B 2400/04 relates to inventions that define or control the shape of slag formed when molten iron or steel waste solidifies, often to improve handling, separation or material recovery. It includes methods and apparatuses that influence slag morphology during cooling, and is situated under chemistry → metallurgy → manufacture of iron or steel → treatment of slags originating from iron or steel processes.
[C21B 2400/042] Sheets -- The CPC code C21B 2400/042 falls under the hierarchy of chemistry, metallurgy and manufacture of iron or steel, specifically dealing with the treatment of slags from iron and steel processes. It classifies sheet-shaped materials or products resulting from such slag-treatment operations.
[C21B 2400/044] Briquettes or moulded bodies other than sheets -- It covers processes for shaping slags produced in iron or steel manufacturing into solid briquettes or other three-dimensional moulded bodies, excluding flat sheets. The entry includes methods of binding, compaction and handling that turn waste slag into reusable or fuel-grade products.
[C21B 2400/05] Apparatus features -- C21B 2400/05 covers the structural and functional characteristics of equipment designed for processing or treating slags generated in iron and steel production. This includes the design of reactors, separators, cooling systems and other mechanical components specifically adapted to handle slag properties.
[C21B 2400/052] including rotating parts -- This subclass covers methods and apparatus for treating slags from iron or steel production that use rotating components such as drums, rotary kilns, or mixers to facilitate slag separation, cooling, or removal. It falls under the broader categories of chemistry, metallurgy and manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21B 2400/054] Disc-shaped or conical parts for cooling, dispersing or atomising of molten slag rotating along vertical axis -- The CPC code C21B 2400/054 pertains to disc-shaped or conical components that rotate about a vertical axis to cool, disperse or atomise molten slag generated in iron or steel manufacturing. These parts are employed in slag-treatment operations to promote solidification and impurity removal.
[C21B 2400/056] Drums whereby slag is poured on or in between -- A drum system for handling molten slag produced in iron-or steel manufacture, where the slag is poured onto the drum surface or into the gaps between adjacent drums. The arrangement cools and solidifies the slag, facilitating its removal, recovery of metal or further processing, and is classified under treatment of slags.
[C21B 2400/058] Rotating beds on which slag is cooled -- Rotating beds used for cooling slags from iron or steel production are engineered to spread molten slag over a moving surface, rapidly reducing its temperature and solidifying it. The rotation maintains continuous contact with fresh slag, enabling efficient heat extraction, easier handling, and potential recovery of metal or mineral content.
[C21B 2400/06] Conveyors on which slag is cooled -- The subclass covers conveyors designed to move slag from iron or steel processes while cooling it, usually by water or air, so that the hot material solidifies and can be handled or further processed.
[C21B 2400/062] Jet nozzles or pressurised fluids for cooling, fragmenting or atomising slag -- The C21B 2400/062 entry covers devices that inject high-pressure jets or fluids onto molten slag in order to cool it, break it into smaller pieces or atomise it, typically during iron and steel production. Such jet nozzles are employed to improve slag handling, promote rapid solidification and facilitate removal or recycling of the by-product.
[C21B 2400/064] Thermally-conductive removable bodies, e.g. balls -- The CPC entry C21B 2400/064 falls under treatment of slags from iron or steel processes and covers thermally-conductive removable bodies such as balls used to enhance heat transfer in slag-treatment operations.
[C21B 2400/066] Receptacle features where the slag is treated -- The code C21B 2400/066 refers to the design of containers used for treating slags generated in iron or steel production. It covers features such as shape, lining, venting and other receptacle characteristics that facilitate slag processing or disposal. This falls under the CPC hierarchy of chemistry, metallurgy, manufacture of iron or steel, and treatment of slags.
[C21B 2400/068] with a sealed or controlled environment -- The subclass C21B 2400/068 covers methods for treating slags generated during iron or steel production that are performed inside a sealed or otherwise controlled atmosphere. It focuses on processes that isolate the slag from the external environment to manage emissions, temperature, or chemical reactions during treatment.
[C21B 2400/07] open to atmosphere -- C21B 2400/07 covers methods for processing slags generated in iron or steel production that are carried out in an open-to-atmosphere environment, such as exposure to ambient air during cooling, drying, or chemical reactions, rather than in sealed or inert-gas reactors.
[C21B 2400/072] Tanks to collect the slag, e.g. water tank -- This subclass covers tanks, such as water tanks, designed to receive and store slags generated during iron or steel production, facilitating their handling and subsequent treatment.
[C21B 2400/074] Tower structures for cooling, being confined but not sealed -- Tower structures for cooling, being confined but not sealed, are vertical installations used in the treatment of slags from iron or steel processes. They partially enclose the slag cooling zone while allowing gas exchange, enhancing heat removal and solidification without fully sealing the system.
[C21B 2400/076] Fluidised bed for cooling -- A fluidised bed for cooling is a device that uses an upward gas flow to suspend solid particles, allowing rapid heat removal from molten slags produced in iron or steel manufacturing. By quickly lowering the temperature, the bed solidifies the slag, improving safety, handling, and preparation for further processing or recycling.
[C21B 2400/08] with energy recovery -- C21B 2400/08 covers methods for treating slags produced during iron or steel manufacturing that include recovering usable energy from the waste material. It addresses processes such as heat extraction, combustion or gasification of slag to generate power or steam, integrating waste-to-energy steps into metallurgical operations.
[C21B 3/00] General features in the manufacture of pig-iron -- C21B 3/00 covers the overall processes and equipment used in producing pig-iron, such as preparing the charge, operating blast furnaces, controlling temperature, removing slag, and handling and casting the molten iron. It addresses general features common to all pig-iron manufacturing methods.
[C21B 3/02] by applying additives, e.g. fluxing agents -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes in which the additives can be added to dry products (e.g. pellets, briquettes), a metal melt or a slag.
[C21B 3/04] Recovery of by-products, e.g. slag -- C21B 3/04 covers processes for extracting and recycling by-products generated during pig-iron production, such as slag, dust or other residues, and converting them into usable materials or disposing of them in an environmentally responsible way. This subclass addresses methods that separate, treat, or re-use these waste streams within the broader context of iron and steel manufacturing.
[C21B 3/06] Treatment of liquid slag -- **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Slag wool -> C03B - Slag stone -> C04B
[C21B 3/08] Cooling slag -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cooling covers both dry and wet methods of cooling.
[C21B 3/10] Slag pots -- C21B 3/10 covers slag pots, vessels employed in pig-iron production to collect and treat molten iron and its slag. They enable removal, cooling and further processing of slag, improving metal quality and protecting furnace linings.
[C21B 5/00] Making pig-iron in the blast furnace -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also the injection of additional (pure) oxygen and additional fuel; automatic control of the process; condition of the cokes or their characterisation; composition and distribution of the charge.
[C21B 5/001] Injecting additional fuel or reducing agents -- This subclass deals with methods of adding extra fuel or reducing agents to the blast furnace during pig-iron production, aiming to improve temperature control, efficiency, or chemical reduction. It includes injection of gases, liquids, or solid materials directly into the furnace charge or hot metal stream.
[C21B 5/002] Heated electrically (plasma) -- The CPC subclass C21B 5/002 refers to metallurgical processes that heat pig-iron or molten iron using electrical energy, especially plasma torches or electric arcs, within a blast furnace or similar vessel. It covers techniques where the high-temperature plasma source is employed to enhance reduction or refine the iron melt.
[C21B 5/003] Injection of pulverulent coal -- C21B 5/003 refers to the process of injecting pulverised coal into a blast furnace during pig-iron production. It is a subcategory of the metallurgy branch dealing with iron and steel manufacturing, specifically detailing coal-based fuel injection to improve furnace efficiency and reduce coke consumption.
[C21B 5/004] Injection of slurries -- The CPC entry C21B 5/004, titled "Injection of slurries," pertains to the process of introducing liquid or semi-liquid mixtures-such as coke, coal, oxygen-bearing, or non-metallic slurries-directly into a blast furnace during pig-iron production. This technique is used to improve fuel efficiency, control furnace temperature, and modify the chemical composition of the melt. It falls under the metallurgy branch of iron and steel manufacturing.
[C21B 5/006] Automatically controlling the process -- C21B 5/006 relates to automatic control systems for the blast-furnace process used in making pig-iron, encompassing sensors, controllers and feedback mechanisms that continuously adjust temperature, pressure, fuel and other operating parameters without manual intervention.
[C21B 5/007] Conditions of the cokes or characterised by the cokes used -- This subclass concerns the specific properties and treatment of the coke used in a blast-furnace process for pig-iron production. It covers how coke characteristics such as size, reactivity, moisture or composition and operating conditions like temperature or feeding rate affect iron reduction.
[C21B 5/008] Composition or distribution of the charge -- This subclass deals with the selection and arrangement of the raw charge fed into a blast furnace for pig-iron production, including the proportion and placement of coke, iron ore, limestone and other additives to control reduction, temperature and fluid flow.
[C21B 5/02] Making special pig-iron, e.g. by applying additives, e.g. oxides of other metals -- This subclass covers processes for producing pig-iron with modified composition by introducing additive materials such as metal oxides during the blast-furnace operation. The additives are used to impart desired properties or to improve the quality of the resulting pig-iron.
[C21B 5/023] Injection of the additives into the melting part -- C21B 5/023 pertains to the manufacture of pig-iron in a blast furnace where additives are injected directly into the molten zone. The classification covers methods of introducing substances such as carbon, fluxes or alloying elements into the melt to modify composition, temperature or fluidity during ironmaking. This falls under the broader hierarchy of chemistry → metallurgy → manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21B 5/026] of plastic material -- C21B 5/026 refers to the use of plastic material in the blast-furnace production of pig-iron, a subprocess of iron and steel manufacturing. It covers methods where plastics serve as fuel, reducing agent or additive during the blast-furnace operation. This subclass falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Manufacture of iron or steel → Making pig-iron in the blast furnace.
[C21B 5/04] Making slag of special composition -- The C21B 5/04 entry covers processes for producing slag with a defined chemical makeup during pig-iron production in a blast furnace. It includes the selection and addition of fluxing agents or other materials to achieve desired slag properties such as viscosity, refractory protection, or impurity removal, and may describe controlling temperature or composition to attain the special slag. This classification falls under metallurgy, specifically the manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21B 5/06] using top gas in the blast furnace process -- C21B 5/06 covers the utilisation of the top gas that is drawn off from the upper part of a blast furnace during pig-iron production. It includes methods for recycling, redirecting or treating this gas to improve furnace efficiency, reduce emissions, or generate heat or power within the iron-making process.
[C21B 7/00] Blast furnaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Features which relate to the lay-out of the BF area or to repair ; also the evacuation and treatment of exhaust gases and the control and regulation of the top pressure.
[C21B 7/002] Evacuating and treating of exhaust gases -- The subclass covers methods and apparatus for removing and treating exhaust gases produced by blast furnaces in iron and steel manufacturing, including gas evacuation, cooling, dust removal and chemical treatment to reduce emissions and recover useful components.
[C21B 7/005] Bleeder valves or slides -- The CPC entry C21B 7/005 covers bleeder valves or slides used in blast furnaces for the controlled release of gases, pressure or slag during iron or steel production. These components enable safe venting and help maintain furnace stability and efficiency.
[C21B 7/007] Controlling or regulating of the top pressure -- The CPC subclass C21B 7/007 covers techniques for controlling or regulating the pressure at the top of a blast furnace during iron or steel production. It includes sensors, pneumatic or hydraulic devices, and control strategies that maintain desired pressure levels to improve furnace efficiency, product quality and safety.
[C21B 7/02] Internal forms -- C21B 7/02 covers the internal forms used in blast furnaces, encompassing the refractory linings, tuyeres, and other shaping structures that define the furnace cavity and direct the flow of gases and molten metal during iron or steel production. These components are designed to withstand high temperatures and chemical attack while maintaining the required geometry for efficient operation.
[C21B 7/04] with special refractories -- C21B 7/04 covers blast-furnace processes that employ special refractory linings or materials to protect the furnace interior from extreme heat, chemical erosion and mechanical wear. It includes the selection, design, installation and maintenance of such refractories to improve furnace efficiency and lifespan.
[C21B 7/06] Linings for furnaces -- The CPC subclass C21B 7/06 covers the design, composition and use of protective linings inside blast furnaces employed in iron or steel manufacturing. It includes refractory materials, coatings and methods for installing or repairing furnace walls to endure extreme temperatures and chemical attack.
[C21B 7/08] Top armourings -- Top armourings are protective refractory linings installed on the upper part of a blast furnace to shield the furnace shell and charge from wear, heat and chemical attack during iron-making operations. They consist of specially formulated bricks or castables that resist erosion by the descending burden and the aggressive gases generated in the furnace. This subclass groups designs, materials and methods used for such top-level protective structures.
[C21B 7/10] Cooling -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Cooling devices for the walls and bottom including staves, plates, pipes, etc; also leakage detection.
[C21B 7/103] Detection of leakages of the cooling liquid -- C21B 7/103 covers techniques for identifying leaks in the water or other cooling liquids that circulate through blast-furnace walls and tuyeres, including sensors, monitoring systems, and diagnostic procedures designed to protect furnace integrity and improve operational safety.
[C21B 7/106] Cooling of the furnace bottom -- The C21B 7/106 subclass covers technologies for removing heat from the bottom of a blast furnace during iron or steel production, including water spray, coolant circulation, cooling panels and related apparatus. It addresses methods that protect the furnace lining, improve thermal stability and enhance overall process efficiency.
[C21B 7/12] Opening or sealing the tap holes -- The code C21B 7/12 covers apparatus, methods and tools used to open or close the tap holes of blast furnaces, which are the openings through which molten iron or slag are drawn. It includes mechanisms for removing plugs, inserting sealing devices and controlling flow during operation.
[C21B 7/125] Refractory plugging mass -- Refractory plugging mass refers to a material placed in blast-furnace hearths, tuyeres or other high-temperature zones to seal gaps, protect linings and control gas flow during operation. The mass typically consists of a mixture of high-temperature-resistant binders and aggregates that harden in situ, maintaining furnace integrity and preventing waste of heat or slag leakage.
[C21B 7/14] Discharging devices, e.g. for slag -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Runners and their accessories (roofs, heating etc); also equipment for transporting said runners.
[C21B 7/16] Tuyéres -- Tuyères are refractory-lined nozzles that inject the blast of hot air or enriched oxygen into a blast furnace, shaping and directing the flow to optimize combustion and reduce temperature gradients. The entry covers their design, materials, cooling methods and installation aspects that affect furnace efficiency and steel production.
[C21B 7/163] Blowpipe assembly -- The C21B 7/163 entry defines blowpipe assemblies employed in blast-furnace operations, encompassing the pipe, nozzle and associated control devices that inject heated air or gas into the furnace hearth to enhance combustion and facilitate impurity removal.
[C21B 7/166] Tuyere replacement apparatus -- A tuyere replacement apparatus is a device used in blast furnaces for iron or steel production to remove an existing tuyere - the pipe that injects air or oxygen - and install a new one safely and efficiently, often with remote or automated mechanisms to minimise furnace downtime and exposure of workers.
[C21B 7/18] Bell-and-hopper arrangements -- C21B 7/18 defines patent subject matter concerning the configuration of bell and hopper systems used in blast furnaces for iron and steel production. The classification addresses the arrangement of these structures that control the flow of solid charge and gas, improving furnace efficiency and tapping operations. It falls under the chemistry-metallurgy hierarchy for manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21B 7/20] with appliances for distributing the burden -- **Definition:** This place covers:  All distribution means different from bell-and-hopper, i.e. including revolving chute.
[C21B 7/205] Details concerning the gear-box driving the charge distribution system -- The code C21B 7/205 concerns the mechanical components that power the charge-distribution system in a blast furnace, specifically the gearbox that drives the equipment feeding raw material into the furnace. It includes the design, operation, control and maintenance of such gear-boxes as part of iron-making processes.
[C21B 7/22] Dust arresters -- C21B 7/22 covers dust arresters used in blast-furnace operations. It includes devices or systems that capture, filter or suppress particulate matter generated during the preparation, charging, or tapping stages of iron and steel production, thereby reducing emissions and improving workplace safety.
[C21B 7/24] Test rods or other checking devices -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Covers any measuring, controlling or observation devices
[C21B 9/00] Stoves for heating the blast in blast furnaces -- Stoves for heating the blast in blast furnaces are devices that generate hot gases, typically by burning fuel, to raise the temperature of the air blown into a blast furnace. By pre-heating the blast, they improve combustion efficiency, increase furnace temperature, and enhance the reduction of iron ore during steel production.
[C21B 9/02] Brick hot-blast stoves -- Brick hot-blast stoves are refractory structures that recover heat from the exhaust gases of a blast furnace and use it to preheat the incoming combustion air for the furnace, thereby increasing fuel efficiency and productivity in iron and steel making. They are constructed mainly from heat-resistant bricks and are classified under C21B 9/02 in the Cooperative Patent Classification system.
[C21B 9/04] with combustion shaft -- The C21B 9/04 subclass deals with stoves used to heat the blast in blast-furnace operations, specifically those that incorporate a combustion shaft in which fuel is burned and the generated heat is transferred to the blast air. This apparatus falls under the manufacture of iron or steel in metallurgical processes.
[C21B 9/06] Linings -- C21B 9/06 covers the design, composition and installation of protective linings for stoves that preheat the blast air in iron and steel blast furnaces. It includes refractory materials, mounting methods and related processes aimed at improving furnace efficiency and durability.
[C21B 9/08] Iron hot-blast stoves -- C21B 9/08 refers to iron hot-blast stoves, devices used in the manufacture of iron or steel to pre-heat the air blast fed into a blast furnace. The stoves store heat from combustion and release it to raise furnace temperature, improving efficiency and productivity.
[C21B 9/10] Other details, e.g. blast mains -- C21B 9/10 relates to auxiliary components used for heating the blast in a blast furnace, specifically items such as blast mains and other ancillary piping or devices that supply or regulate the hot air or gas stream. It covers the design, arrangement and construction details of these support structures rather than the furnace body itself. This subclass falls under manufacture of iron or steel within the metallurgy section of the CPC.
[C21B 9/12] Hot-blast valves or slides for blast furnaces -- C21B 9/12 covers hot-blast valves or slides used in blast furnaces, devices that regulate the flow of preheated air (the hot blast) into the furnace during iron or steel production. These components are part of the stove system that heats the blast, ensuring proper temperature and pressure control for efficient metallurgical processes.
[C21B 9/14] Preheating the combustion air -- This CPC subclass is part of chemistry-metallurgy-manufacture of iron or steel and deals with stoves used to heat the blast in blast furnaces. It covers methods and apparatus for preheating the combustion air supplied to the furnace, which improves efficiency and reduces fuel consumption.
[C21B 9/16] Cooling or drying the hot-blast -- C21B 9/16 relates to methods and apparatus for cooling or drying the hot-blast used in iron or steel making, typically involving stoves that heat the blast in a blast furnace. It falls under the metallurgy hierarchy for manufacture of iron or steel.
[C21C] PROCESSING OF PIG-IRON, e.g. REFINING, MANUFACTURE OF WROUGHT-IRON OR STEEL -- **Definition:** This place covers:  all treatments of molten iron or steel, including the apparatuses specifically related thereto, e.g. converter, electric furnace.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cast iron alloys -> C22C37/00 - Ferrous alloy compositions -> C22C38/00
[C21C 1/00] Refining of pig-iron -- The CPC class C21C 1/00 covers processes for refining pig-iron, focusing on the removal of impurities and adjustment of composition before further steelmaking. It includes methods such as oxygen blowing, basic slag treatment and other chemical or metallurgical techniques used to convert raw molten iron into higher-quality metal.
[C21C 1/02] Dephosphorising or desulfurising -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also the specific treating agents
[C21C 1/025] Agents used for dephosphorising or desulfurising -- C21C 1/025 covers chemical additives employed in the refining of pig-iron to lower its phosphorus or sulfur content, improving the metal's quality for subsequent steelmaking. The agents may be solids, liquids or gases that react with or bind the undesired elements, facilitating their removal during dephosphorising or desulfurising processes.
[C21C 1/04] Removing impurities other than carbon, phosphorus or sulfur -- The CPC subclass C21C 1/04 concerns refining pig-iron by removing impurities that are not carbon, phosphorus or sulfur. It includes methods such as oxidation, slagging or other treatments that selectively eliminate metallic or non-metallic contaminants while leaving the main alloying elements unchanged. This subclass falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Processing of pig-iron.
[C21C 1/06] Constructional features of mixers for pig-iron -- C21C 1/06 covers the design and structural elements of mixing equipment used in the refining of pig-iron, including the arrangement of paddles, chambers, drive mechanisms and any specific adaptations that improve the efficiency or control of the mixing process during steel production.
[C21C 1/08] Manufacture of cast-iron -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Treatment of pig iron to obtain non-spheroidal cast-iron.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Cast-iron alloys (composition) -> C22C37/00 - C22C37/10
[C21C 1/10] Making spheroidal graphite cast-iron -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also the nodularising agents
[C21C 1/105] Nodularising additive agents -- C21C 1/105 refers to chemical additive agents applied in the refining of pig-iron to promote nodular, or spheroidal, graphite formation, which enhances the ductility and overall mechanical performance of the resulting steel.
[C21C 2005/363] Slag cements -- C21C 2005/363 covers cement compositions that incorporate ground granulated blast-furnace slag as a principal binder component, methods for producing such slag cements, and their use in concrete or mortar formulations to improve durability, reduce heat of hydration, and lower the carbon footprint of construction materials.
[C21C 2005/366] Foam slags -- Foam slags are foamed or cellular metallic slags produced as a by-product of metallurgical processes and subsequently processed into lightweight, porous material. The classification covers methods for producing such foamed slags, their treatment, and their use in construction, insulation, demolition or as aggregates. It includes compositions, shaping techniques and applications where the material's low density and thermal properties are exploited.
[C21C 2005/446] Dry linings -- C21C 2005/446 - Dry linings refers to the application of coating or lining materials that are applied in a dry state, such as powders, films, sheets or powders that are later fused, sintered or otherwise solidified to form a protective or functional layer on the interior or exterior of containers, pipes, tanks or other structures.
[C21C 2005/448] Lining wear indicators -- It covers indicators that detect or signal the wear of a lining in equipment such as furnaces, boilers or other lined components, including visual, mechanical or electronic markers that reveal when the protective lining has degraded.
[C21C 2005/4626] Means for cooling, e.g. by gases, fluids or liquids -- C21C 2005/4626 covers apparatus and components that provide cooling by the circulation of gases, fluids or liquids, including refrigeration units, heat-exchangers, cooling channels and related control devices used to remove heat from a system or product. It focuses on the means for achieving temperature reduction rather than the specific cooling medium itself.
[C21C 2005/4666] for charging with organic contaminated scrap -- C21C 2005/4666 covers methods for charging processing equipment with scrap that is contaminated by organic material. It is used in recycling or recovery operations where metal or other substances are separated from organic-laden waste before further treatment.
[C21C 2005/468] Means for determining the weight of the converter -- C21C 2005/468 covers apparatus or systems designed to measure or assess the weight of a converter, such as a power-electronic or mechanical unit, often for monitoring performance, safety, or balance during operation or testing. The classification applies to sensors, weighing mechanisms, and associated electronics that provide a weight reading of the converter itself.
[C21C 2005/5223] with post-combustion -- C21C 2005/5223 is a CPC subclass in the carbonization group that specifies processes which incorporate a post-combustion stage, such as treating the carbonized material or its off-gas after the primary carbonization step to improve fuel quality, remove impurities or capture CO₂.
[C21C 2005/5235] with bottom electrodes -- C21C 2005/5235 covers metal-coating or plating processes in which the coated item incorporates a bottom electrode, typically for electronic components such as capacitors, batteries or sensors. It includes methods for forming the electrode layer, the materials employed and related manufacturing steps that integrate the electrode beneath subsequent layers.
[C21C 2005/5258] with crater formed by down-melting of scrap or charge through electrode or lance -- The CPC subclass C21C 2005/5258 pertains to electric-arc furnaces or similar melting operations in which a crater is created by the downward melting of scrap metal or charge material through an electrode or a lance, influencing the flow of molten metal and slag. It covers the specific configuration and effects of such cratering during the melting process.
[C21C 2005/5276] with liquid or solid rest, e.g. pool, "sumpf" -- This CPC subgroup covers processes for preparing inorganic chemicals in which the reaction zone includes a liquid or solid reservoir, such as a pool or sump, that acts as a rest for material handling, heat exchange, or catalyst retention. It includes operations where the product or intermediates are collected in the reservoir during or after the reaction.
[C21C 2005/5282] with organic contaminated scrap -- The CPC subclass C21C 2005/5282 covers processes for recovering metals from scrap that is contaminated with organic substances such as oils, greases or polymers. It includes pretreatment steps to remove or neutralize the organic contaminants before metallurgical treatment. Applications typically address environmental and efficiency aspects of handling polluted scrap streams.
[C21C 2005/5288] Measuring or sampling devices -- The CPC entry C21C 2005/5288 refers to measuring or sampling devices used in metalworking and related processes. It includes instruments such as gauges, testers, probes and sampling apparatus that determine dimensions, properties or composition of workpieces, and is applied in quality-control, process monitoring and material analysis.
[C21C 2007/0012] Lead -- C21C 2007/0012 concerns the production and processing of lead, including its extraction, refining, alloying and recycling. The entry covers metallurgical methods for obtaining metallic lead and preparing lead-based alloys, as well as related treatments used in applications such as batteries, radiation shielding and soldering.
[C21C 2007/0018] Boron -- This CPC subclass concerns the use of boron or boron-containing compounds in the production or modification of metallic powders and alloys, including alloying, coating or treating powders with boron to impart specific properties such as hardness or corrosion resistance.
[C21C 2007/0031] being plastics, organic compounds, polymers -- The CPC class C21C 2007/0031 pertains to inventions involving plastics and other organic polymeric compounds, including their composition, synthesis, and processing. It covers synthetic polymers, resinous materials and related organic substances used as plastics, as well as methods for producing and shaping them.
[C21C 2007/0062] with introduction of alloying or treating agents under a compacted form different from a wire, e.g. briquette, pellet -- The code refers to processes that introduce alloying or treating agents into a metal that is compacted into shapes other than wire, such as briquettes or pellets. It covers the preparation, treatment and modification of these compacted forms to achieve desired properties before further manufacturing steps.
[C21C 2007/0093] Duplex process;  Two stage processes -- C21C 2007/0093 defines a duplex or two-stage process for preparing polymers, in which the reaction is carried out in separate stages that can differ in temperature, pressure, catalyst or monomer feed, enabling sequential polymerisation steps to achieve specific polymer characteristics.
[C21C 2100/00] Exhaust gas -- The C21C 2100/00 entry covers technologies for handling the exhaust gas generated during pig-iron processing, such as refining, casting or steelmaking. It includes methods for cleaning, recovering, treating or otherwise utilizing the gases emitted in metallurgical operations. This sub-class falls under chemistry → metallurgy → processing of pig-iron.
[C21C 2100/02] Treatment of the exhaust gas -- The subclass C21C 2100/02 covers methods and apparatus for treating exhaust gases produced during pig-iron processing, such as smelting, refining and steel manufacturing. It includes techniques for removing dust, sulfur compounds, nitrogen oxides and other pollutants, as well as catalytic conversion, gas scrubbing and heat-recovery processes applied to metallurgical exhaust streams.
[C21C 2100/04] Recirculation of the exhaust gas -- The CPC subclass C21C 2100/04 covers techniques for taking the exhaust gases generated during pig-iron processing and feeding them back into the furnace or other parts of the metallurgical plant. It includes methods that recycle these gases to improve energy efficiency, control the furnace atmosphere, and lower emissions while influencing the chemistry of the molten iron.
[C21C 2100/06] Energy from waste gas used in other processes -- This CPC subclass deals with using energy derived from waste gases as a supplemental power source in other industrial processes, particularly within pig-iron processing and related metallurgical operations. It covers methods that capture exhaust-gas heat or combustible components and redirect it to drive equipment or heating steps elsewhere in the plant.
[C21C 2200/00] Recycling of waste material -- C21C 2200/00 pertains to methods for recycling waste material in pig-iron processing, including the recovery, treatment and reuse of metal residues, slags and other by-products during refining or the manufacture of wrought-iron or steel.
[C21C 2250/00] Specific additives -- C21C 2250/00 "Specific additives" is a CPC entry under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Processing of pig-iron, covering the use of particular chemical or metallic additives during pig-iron refining or in the manufacture of wrought-iron and steel to modify composition, improve properties, or facilitate downstream processing.
[C21C 2250/02] Hot oxygen -- C21C 2250/02 covers the use of hot-oxygen as a specific additive in the processing of pig-iron, including refining and the manufacture of wrought iron or steel. It relates to methods where oxygen is introduced in a heated state to improve the efficiency or quality of the metallurgical process.
[C21C 2250/04] Liquid gas -- The CPC subclass C21C 2250/04 relates to the introduction of liquid gases as specific additives during the processing of pig-iron, including refining and the manufacture of wrought-iron or steel. It covers methods that employ gases in liquid form to influence melt chemistry, temperature control, or deoxidation within metallurgical operations.
[C21C 2250/042] Liquid oxygen -- C21C 2250/042 covers the use of liquid oxygen as a specific additive in the metallurgical processing of pig-iron, such as refining or producing wrought-iron and steel. It applies to methods and apparatus where liquid oxygen is introduced to improve combustion, oxidation or temperature control during these processes.
[C21C 2250/06] Hollow electrode -- C21C 2250/06 designates hollow electrodes used as specific additives in the processing of pig-iron, such as refining or the manufacture of wrought iron and steel. The code covers electrodes that are internally hollow to allow gas flow or cooling, improving efficiency and control during electric melting or casting operations. It falls under the metallurgy hierarchy for processing of pig-iron.
[C21C 2250/08] Porous plug -- C21C 2250/08 pertains to porous plugs employed as specific additives in the processing of pig-iron, refining, or the manufacture of wrought iron and steel, where the plug's porous structure is used to control flow, filter material, or modify reaction conditions during metallurgical operations.
[C21C 2300/00] Process aspects -- C21C 2300/00 pertains to the process aspects of pig-iron processing, covering methods for refining pig-iron and converting it into wrought iron or steel. It resides within the hierarchy of chemistry, metallurgy and the broader field of processing pig-iron.
[C21C 2300/02] Foam creation -- The CPC subclass C21C 2300/02 relates to techniques for generating a foam in the processing of pig-iron, such as during refining or casting of wrought iron and steel. It includes the addition of foaming agents or gas injection to create a stable metallic foam that influences solidification, heat transfer or impurity removal.
[C21C 2300/04] Avoiding foam formation -- The entry covers methods for preventing foam formation during pig-iron processing steps such as refining or the manufacture of wrought iron and steel. It includes techniques to control gas evolution, adjust temperature or chemical composition, and modify agitation or reaction conditions to keep the melt free of stable foams.
[C21C 2300/06] Modeling of the process, e.g. for control purposes -- C21C 2300/06 covers the creation of mathematical or computer models of pig-iron processing steps such as refining or the manufacture of wrought-iron and steel, primarily to simulate, predict or optimise operating conditions for process control. It is used for designing control systems and improving efficiency in metallurgical operations.
[C21C 2300/08] Particular sequence of the process steps -- The CPC entry C21C 2300/08 concerns inventions that define a specific order in which the individual steps of pig-iron processing-such as refining, de-oxidation, heating, or shaping-are carried out. By prescribing a particular sequence of operations, the patent aims to improve efficiency, product quality, or economic performance in the manufacture of wrought iron or steel.
[C21C 3/00] Manufacture of wrought-iron or wrought-steel -- The C21C 3/00 subclass covers all steps involved in turning pig-iron into wrought-iron or wrought-steel, including refining, decarburisation, alloying, and shaping operations such as rolling, forging or drawing. It addresses the complete conversion process from raw pig-iron to the finished malleable metal.
[C21C 5/00] Manufacture of carbon-steel, e.g. plain mild steel, medium carbon steel or cast steel -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also the manufacturing of stainless steels and ferro-alloys; apparatuses, in particular converters, which are specifically dedicated to the steel processing are classified within this group as well  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Ferrous alloy compositions -> C22C38/00 - C22C38/60
[C21C 5/005] Manufacture of stainless steel -- The CPC subclass C21C 5/005 deals with methods for producing stainless steel, a corrosion-resistant alloy typically containing chromium, nickel and other elements. It includes steps such as melting, refining, alloying and casting of carbon-steel to obtain the final stainless composition.
[C21C 5/02] Crucible furnace process -- C21C 5/02 refers to the crucible-furnace method used in the production of carbon-steel, covering processes where molten pig-iron or steel is melted, refined, and alloyed in a sealed crucible to achieve the desired composition and properties. This falls under the metallurgy sub-class dealing with processing of pig-iron and manufacture of wrought-iron or steel.
[C21C 5/04] Manufacture of hearth-furnace steel, e.g. Siemens-Martin steel -- This CPC entry C21C 5/04 falls under chemistry and metallurgy, in the processing of pig-iron and the manufacture of carbon-steel. It concerns the production of hearth-furnace steel, such as Siemens-Martin steel, including plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel made in a furnace.
[C21C 5/06] Processes yielding slags of special composition -- The C21C 5/06 subclass concerns methods used in carbon-steel manufacture that generate slags with specific chemical or physical characteristics, such as tailored composition for improved metal recovery, impurity removal, or environmental performance during pig-iron refining and steel processing.
[C21C 5/28] Manufacture of steel in the converter -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Also the full plant lay-out.
[C21C 5/285] Plants therefor -- The C21C 5/285 subgroup covers the plant structures, equipment and integrated process units used to produce carbon-steel from pig-iron, encompassing furnaces, rolling mills, casting lines, heat-treatment sections and related auxiliary systems required for refining and shaping plain, medium-carbon or cast steel.
[C21C 5/30] Regulating or controlling the blowing -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Converter processes in which the regulation or control of the blowing is claimed, be it from above, through the bath or a combination thereof, i.e. not specific to one of the methods ; the regulation or control can relate to the amount, the sequence, the composition etc of the gases.  Also post-combustion is considered as a means to control the blowing
[C21C 5/305] Afterburning -- Afterburning is a supplementary combustion stage used in the manufacture of carbon-steel, where gases or carbon-rich residues from the primary furnace are further ignited to raise temperature, improve thermal efficiency and help reduce excess carbon in the melt. This process is applied after the main refining steps in steel production.
[C21C 5/32] Blowing from above -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Regulation or control of blowing ONLY from above, i.e. through a lance  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Lance details -> C21C5/46 , F27D3/16 , F27D3/18
[C21C 5/34] Blowing through the bath -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Regulation or control of blowing only through the melt, i.e. through a tuyere or bottom  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Tuyere details -> C21C5/48 , B22D1/005
[C21C 5/35] Blowing from above and through the bath -- The CPC sub-group C21C 5/35 covers steel-making methods where gas is blown from above and through the molten bath to aid refining, temperature control or chemical reactions during the manufacture of carbon-steel.
[C21C 5/36] Processes yielding slags of special composition -- C21C 5/36 covers methods for producing slags with deliberately tailored chemical makeup during the processing of pig-iron into carbon-steel products such as mild, medium-carbon or cast steel. The processes aim to control slag properties for improved metal quality, deoxidation, alloying or impurity removal.
[C21C 5/38] Removal of waste gases or dust -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The treatment of the off-gas
[C21C 5/40] Offtakes or separating apparatus for converter waste gases or dust -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The installation required for capturing and treating of the off-gas.
[C21C 5/42] Constructional features of converters -- This subclass covers the design and structural aspects of converters used in steelmaking, such as shape, lining and internal components that affect the conversion of pig iron to carbon steel. It includes modifications to improve heat-transfer, slag handling and gas flow within the vessel.
[C21C 5/44] Refractory linings -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Apart from the lining itself, the equipment to make, apply or repair the lining, both of the vessel and of the taphole in particular.
[C21C 5/441] Equipment used for making or repairing linings -- C21C 5/441 designates equipment used to install, replace or repair internal linings of vessels involved in pig-iron processing and carbon-steel production, such as ladles, converters or molds. It covers tools, machines and handling devices specifically intended for lining work in steelmaking.
[C21C 5/443] Hot fettling; Flame gunning -- The CPC subclass C21C 5/443 covers hot-working finishing operations on carbon-steel products, specifically hot fettling and flame-gunning techniques used to remove scale, surface defects or excess material after casting or shaping. These processes are applied during the manufacture of plain, medium-carbon or cast steel.
[C21C 5/445] Lining or repairing the taphole -- This CPC entry covers methods and materials used to line or restore the taphole through which molten iron passes in a blast furnace or similar vessel. It includes techniques for applying refractory linings, repairing damage, and maintaining taphole integrity during steelmaking.
[C21C 5/46] Details or accessories -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Lances, means for their handling; supporting means for the converter; cooling arrangements; tapholes, their opening and sealing; charging devices; measuring and sampling devices; support and transport devices for the converter; cleaning and skull removal.
[C21C 5/4606] Lances or injectors -- C21C 5/4606 classifies lances or injectors used in the metallurgical processing of pig-iron to produce carbon-steel such as mild, medium-carbon or cast steel. The entry covers devices that introduce gases, oxygen or fuel into furnaces or converters to assist refining and steel making.
[C21C 5/4613] Refractory coated lances; Immersion lances -- The classification covers refractory-coated lances and immersion lances employed in the refining and processing of pig-iron and the manufacture of carbon steel, where the lances are lined with heat-resistant material to withstand molten metal and are inserted into the bath to stir, heat or introduce gases, improving control of temperature and chemistry during steel production.
[C21C 5/462] Means for handling, e.g. adjusting, changing, coupling -- The C21C 5/462 entry designates devices used in the manufacture of carbon-steel that facilitate handling operations such as adjusting, changing or coupling material, tools or work-pieces during processing. It covers fixtures, manipulators, coupling mechanisms and similar equipment employed in refining or shaping steel products.
[C21C 5/4633] Supporting means -- C21C 5/4633 refers to supporting means used in the processing of pig-iron into carbon-steel products such as plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel. It covers devices, fixtures or structures that hold, guide or support the material during refining, rolling, shaping or other manufacturing steps to ensure proper handling and dimensional control.
[C21C 5/464] Trunnion bearings -- C21C 5/464 covers trunnion bearings used in the processing of pig-iron and the manufacture of carbon-steel, such as plain mild, medium carbon or cast steel. The classification applies to bearing designs that support rotating or pivoting shafts in rolling, refining or other metallurgical operations, ensuring proper load handling and alignment during steel production.
[C21C 5/4646] Cooling arrangements -- C21C 5/4646 covers the cooling arrangements used during the manufacture of carbon-steel, such as plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel. It falls under the metallurgy sub-field of processing pig-iron, specifically the refining and production steps that shape wrought-iron or steel into final carbon-steel products. This classification addresses methods and apparatus for controlling temperature as steel solidifies or is formed.
[C21C 5/4653] Tapholes; Opening or plugging thereof -- C21C 5/4653 concerns tapholes, the openings used to tap molten metal from furnaces or molds, and the methods for opening, enlarging, maintaining or plugging them during the processing and refining of pig-iron and carbon-steel.
[C21C 5/466] Charging device for converters -- This CPC subclass covers devices used to charge molten metal into converters during steelmaking, typically for refining pig-iron into carbon steel. It includes ladles, torpedo cars and automated feeding systems that supply raw material to basic-oxygen or electric furnaces.
[C21C 5/4673] Measuring and sampling devices -- C21C 5/4673 covers measuring and sampling devices used in the processing of pig-iron and the manufacture of carbon-steel, such as plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel. The class includes instruments for monitoring composition, temperature, flow or other parameters during refining, casting or rolling operations.
[C21C 5/4686] Vehicles for supporting and transporting a converter vessel -- This CPC entry covers vehicles designed to support and transport converter vessels used in the processing of pig-iron and steel production. It includes carriage, wheeled or tracked transporters and supporting frames that move, position, or rotate converters during refining, tapping, or casting operations.
[C21C 5/4693] Skull removal; Cleaning of the converter mouth -- The subclass deals with techniques for eliminating the solidified steel deposit, called the skull, that forms at the bottom of a steel converter and for cleaning the mouth of the converter to enable continuous operation. It is applied in carbon-steel production processes such as refining pig iron.
[C21C 5/48] Bottoms or tuyéres of converters -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Porous plugs and tuyeres
[C21C 5/50] Tilting mechanisms for converters -- C21C 5/50 refers to tilting mechanisms for converters employed in the processing of pig-iron, such as the refining steps and the manufacture of carbon-steel products including mild, medium-carbon and cast steel.
[C21C 5/52] Manufacture of steel in electric furnaces -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Any type of electric heating : AC, DC, induction or plasma, incl. accessories as burners.  The manufacturing of alloyed steels, incl. ferro-alloys.  The charging of the electric furnace.  Multiple hearth furnaces.  The general lay-out of the melt shop.
[C21C 5/5205] in a plasma heated furnace -- C21C 5/5205 covers the manufacture of carbon steel in which the heating step is performed in a plasma heated furnace. This method uses a high-temperature plasma to melt pig iron or steel scrap, enabling rapid heating and refined control of composition and temperature during refining and casting.
[C21C 5/5211] in an alternating current [AC] electric arc furnace -- C21C 5/5211 covers the use of an alternating-current electric arc furnace for refining pig-iron and producing carbon-steel such as plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel. The method belongs to the metallurgy subclass dealing with processing of pig-iron into wrought iron or steel.
[C21C 5/5217] equipped with burners or devices for injecting gas, i.e. oxygen, or pulverulent materials into the furnace -- The CPC subclass C21C 5/5217 covers steel-making furnaces that are fitted with burners or devices for injecting gases such as oxygen or pulverulent materials into the melt. It applies to processes used in the manufacture of carbon-steel, including refining pig-iron and producing wrought-iron or steel, where gas or powder injection aids the reaction.
[C21C 5/5229] in a direct current [DC] electric arc furnace -- The CPC subclass C21C 5/5229 deals with the use of a direct-current (DC) electric-arc furnace in the production of carbon-steel, such as plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel, as part of pig-iron processing and steel-making operations.
[C21C 5/5241] in an inductively heated furnace -- The subclass C21C 5/5241 deals with producing carbon-steel, such as plain mild, medium-carbon or cast steel, by using an inductively heated furnace during the refining or casting stage. It belongs to the hierarchy of chemistry → metallurgy → processing of pig-iron, e.g. refining and manufacture of wrought-iron or steel.
[C21C 5/5247] processing a moving metal stream while exposed to an electromagnetic field, e.g. in an electromagnetic counter current channel -- This CPC subclass covers methods for treating a flowing metal stream by applying an electromagnetic field, such as in an electromagnetic counter-current channel, during the production of carbon-steel products like plain, medium-carbon or cast steel. It relates to continuous refining or shaping operations where the metal is electrically influenced while moving.
[C21C 5/5252] in an electrically heated multi-chamber furnace, a combination of electric furnaces or an electric furnace arranged for associated working with a non electric furnace
[C21C 5/5264] Manufacture of alloyed steels including ferro-alloys -- This CPC subclass C21C 5/5264 relates to the manufacturing of alloyed steels, where ferro-alloys or other alloying elements are introduced into carbon-steel melts to produce steels with controlled composition and enhanced properties. The processes covered include melting, refining, alloy addition, casting and subsequent heat-treatment steps typical of steel production.
[C21C 5/527] Charging of the electric furnace -- C21C 5/527 deals with the charging of electric furnaces used in the production of carbon steel, including the introduction of raw iron, scrap or alloying elements into the melt. The subclass falls under processing of pig-iron and covers the handling and feeding techniques that prepare material for refining or casting.
[C21C 5/5294] General arrangement or layout of the electric melt shop -- The code C21C 5/5294 covers inventions that address the overall arrangement and floor layout of an electric melt shop used in processing pig-iron into carbon steel.
