[C21D 9/665] inverted or side-facing -- C21D 9/665 concerns heat-treatment operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering that are carried out with the workpiece positioned inverted or with its side facing the heat source, allowing specific temperature gradients or surface effects for particular articles.
[C21D 9/667] Multi-station furnaces -- Multi-station furnaces are industrial heat-treatment units that process several ferrous metal articles simultaneously, providing controlled annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering cycles tailored to the specific requirements of each piece. They are classified under CPC code C21D 9/667 within the hierarchy of Chemistry → Metallurgy → Modifying the physical structure of ferrous metals → Heat treatment adapted for particular articles.
[C21D 9/67] adapted for treating the charge in vacuum or special atmosphere -- This subclass covers heat-treatment operations on ferrous metals-annealing, hardening, quenching, tempering-when the charge is processed in a vacuum or a specially controlled atmosphere to avoid oxidation or contamination, adapting the thermal cycle to the inert environment.
[C21D 9/673] Details, accessories, or equipment peculiar to bell-type furnaces -- C21D 9/673 concerns the specific components, accessories and ancillary equipment designed for bell-type furnaces used in heat-treating ferrous metals, such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering processes. It addresses details that are unique to the bell furnace architecture, enabling precise control of temperature and atmosphere for the treatment of steel and related alloys.
[C21D 9/675] Arrangements of charging or discharging devices -- C21D 9/675 covers the layout and configuration of equipment that supplies electrical energy to or removes it from workpieces during heat-treatment operations on ferrous metals, such as charging and discharging arrangements for annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering processes.
[C21D 9/677] Arrangements of heating devices -- It relates to the specific layout and configuration of heating apparatus employed in heat-treatment operations such as annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering of ferrous metal articles. The subclass defines how furnaces, burners, induction coils or other heaters are arranged to achieve the desired thermal cycle.
[C21D 9/68] Furnace coilers -- C21D 9/68 covers furnace coilers, equipment that forms coil shapes in heating furnaces used for annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering of ferrous metal parts. These devices help control the thermal environment and geometry of the furnace to suit specific articles during heat-treatment processes.
[C21D 9/70] Furnaces for ingots, i.e. soaking pits -- C21D 9/70 covers furnaces designed for heating ingots, such as soaking pits, used in heat-treatment operations like annealing, hardening, quenching or tempering of ferrous metals. These installations provide controlled temperature environments to modify the physical structure of the metal before further processing.
[C22] METALLURGY -- C22 encompasses the production and processing of metals, including extraction, refining, alloying, and treatment methods such as smelting, leaching, electrolysis and physical shaping. It also covers apparatus and equipment used in these metallurgical operations.
[C22B] PRODUCTION AND REFINING OF METALS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Metallurgical or chemical processes for producing or recovering metals from metal compounds, ores, waste or scrap metal and for refining metal. Included in this subclass are processes drawn to:  the production of metal by smelting, roasting or furnace method;  the extraction of metal compounds from ore and concentrates by wet processes;  electrochemical treatment of ores and metallurgical products for obtaining metals or alloys; apparatus thereof;  preliminary treatment of ores, concentrates and scrap;  general process for refining or remelting metals;  apparatus for electroslag or arc remelting of metals;  obtaining specific metals;  consolidating metalliferous charges or treating agents that are subsequently used in other processes of this subclass, by agglomerating, compacting, indurating or sintering.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Flotation of ores -> B03D - Working metallic powder; manufacture of articles from metallic powder; making metallic powder -> B22F9/00 - Silicon -> C01B33/02 - Manufacture of iron and steel -> C21B - Processing of pig-iron, manufacture of wrought iron or steel, treatment in molten state of ferrous alloys -> C21C - Electrolytic production or refining of metals -> C25C  **Glossary:** - Carburizing: Treatment of a metal with an externally supplied source of carbon resulting in the chemical reaction or diffusion of the carbon into the metal. - Decarburization: Treatment of a metal to remove carbon therefrom. - Hydrometallurgy: A generic term for processes involving solution in water or other liquid in which metalliferous material or metal is treated to prepare metal, to purify or to refine metal or to prepare intermediate materials more suitable for use in preparing metal (e.g. extracting, leaching, beneficiating, etc.) - Leaching: Extraction by dissolving soluble constituents from insoluble materials. Either the extracted solution or the insoluble material may contain the desired metalliferous material from which metal is obtained. - Pyrometallurgy: A generic term for processes carried out at relatively high temperatures, usually in furnaces, in which metalliferous material or metal is treated to prepare metal, to purify or to refine free metal, or to prepare intermediate materials more suitable for use in preparing metals (e.g. smelting, roasting, etc) - Reducing: Changing from a higher to a lower oxidation state such as, for example, from ferric to ferrous state or to the elemental state - Refining: Purification of metal by removal of impurities therefrom. - Roasting: The treatment of an ore or concentrate with heat and causing partial or full oxidation of the reactive species present in the ore or concentrate to facilitate metal extraction. - Slag: A vitreous mass that separates from fused metals during smelting or refining of metalliferous material. - Smelting: Treatment of metalliferous material, typically a metal sulfide ore or concentrate, with sufficient heat to cause melting of the sulfide mineral(s) in the ore or concentrate such that a molten metal sulfide phase is formed.
[C22B 1/00] Preliminary treatment of ores or scrap -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Roasting processes ( C22B1/02 - C22B1/10 ).  Removing sulfur, phosphorus or arsenic other than by roasting ( C22B1/11 ).  Agglomerating; Briquetting; Binding; Granulating ( C22B1/14 - C22B1/248 ).  Cooling of roasted, sintered and agglomerated ore ( C22B1/26 ).
[C22B 1/005] Preliminary treatment of scrap  C22B1/02  -  C22B1/26  take precedence -- C22B 1/005 covers the preliminary treatment of scrap metal, including sorting, dismantling, cleaning, size reduction and removal of contaminants before melting or further refining. The code is used in the Cooperative Patent Classification to index patents that describe these early preparation steps which improve the efficiency and quality of subsequent metallurgical processes.
[C22B 1/02] Roasting processes -- C22B 1/02 covers roasting processes used in the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap, a subset of metallurgical operations for producing and refining metals. Roasting involves heating the material in the presence of air or oxygen to drive off unwanted components, oxidize the ore, or alter its chemical composition before further processing.
[C22B 1/04] Blast roasting -- C22B 1/04 concerns blast roasting, a preliminary treatment of ores or scrap in which the material is heated in a furnace with an excess of oxygen to oxidize and remove sulfur, carbon or other unwanted constituents before further metallurgical processing.
[C22B 1/06] Sulfating roasting -- Sulfating roasting involves heating sulfide ores or scrap metal in the presence of oxygen and a sulfur-bearing agent, typically sulfur dioxide, to convert sulfides into soluble sulfates and release metal oxides. The process facilitates subsequent leaching or reduction steps by producing a more reactive material and separating unwanted gangue components. It is used in the early stage of metal production for ores such as copper, lead and zinc.
[C22B 1/08] Chloridising roasting -- Chloridising roasting is a preliminary metallurgical treatment where ores or scrap are heated in an oxidising atmosphere containing chlorine or chloride compounds. The process converts metal constituents into volatile metal chlorides, facilitating subsequent extraction or refining steps. It is commonly used for base and precious metals to improve leaching efficiency.
[C22B 1/10] in fluidised form -- The subclass covers preliminary metallurgical treatment in which ores or scrap are handled in a fluidised state, for example in a fluidised-bed reactor, to enable size reduction, mixing, heating or chemical reactions before further processing. It is part of the C22B series dealing with the initial processing of metallic materials.
[C22B 11/00] Obtaining noble metals -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Obtaining noble metals by dry methods ( C22B11/02 - C22B11/028 ).  Obtaining noble metals by wet methods ( C22B11/04 - C22B11/048 ).  Chloridising and cyaniding ( C22B11/06 and C22B11/08 ).  Amalgamating and the apparatus thereof ( C22B11/10 and C22B11/12 ).
[C22B 11/02] by dry processes -- C22B 11/02 deals with the production of noble metals through dry processes, meaning the extraction or purification is carried out without liquid media. Techniques include roasting, calcination, reduction in the solid state, sublimation or mechanical separation to isolate metals like gold, platinum or palladium.
[C22B 11/021] Recovery of noble metals from waste materials -- C22B 11/021 covers techniques for recovering noble metals such as gold, silver and platinum-group elements from waste streams and discarded products. The classification includes chemical, electrolytic, pyrometallurgical and biological methods that separate and concentrate these metals for reuse. It falls under the CPC hierarchy Chemistry - Metallurgy - Production and Refining of Metals - Obtaining noble metals.
[C22B 11/023] from pyrometallurgical residues, e.g. from ashes, dross, flue dust, mud, skim, slag, sludge -- C22B 11/023 covers processes for extracting noble metals from pyrometallurgical waste streams, including ashes, dross, flue dust, mud, skim, slag and sludge. It falls under chemistry, metallurgy and the production and refining of metals, specifically the subcategory dealing with obtaining noble metals. The classification addresses recovery techniques that treat high-temperature metallurgical residues to isolate valuable precious metals.
[C22B 11/025] from manufactured products, e.g. from printed circuit boards, from photographic films, paper, or baths -- C22B 11/025 covers processes for recovering noble metals from waste streams of manufactured items, including printed circuit boards, photographic film, paper and chemical baths. The methods involve extraction, leaching or other treatments to separate valuable metals such as gold, silver or platinum from these secondary sources.
[C22B 11/026] from spent catalysts -- C22B 11/026 addresses methods for extracting noble metals from spent catalytic materials, including leaching, precipitation and thermal treatments used to recover metals such as platinum, palladium, rhodium, gold and silver from waste catalysts in industrial processes.
[C22B 11/028] using solid sorbents, e.g. getters or catchment gauzes -- This subclass covers metallurgical processes for obtaining noble metals in which solid sorbents-such as getters or catch-ment gauzes-are used to trap metal ions or particles from solutions or vapors, enabling their separation and purification. It falls under the CPC hierarchy Chemistry → Metallurgy → Production and refining of metals → Obtaining noble metals.
[C22B 11/04] by wet processes  extraction of metal compounds by leaching in organic solutions  C22B3/16 ; treatment or purification of solutions by liquid-liquid extraction  C22B3/26 -- C22B 11/04 covers wet-process methods for obtaining noble metals in which metal compounds are leached with organic liquids, followed by treatment or purification of the resulting solutions using liquid-liquid extraction techniques. This subclass groups processes that combine organic leaching and solvent-based separation to recover precious metals.
[C22B 11/042] Recovery of noble metals from waste materials -- This subgroup covers techniques for extracting precious metals from discarded or secondary sources, including electronic waste, catalytic converters, and industrial residues. It includes chemical leaching, pyrometallurgical treatment, electrolytic recovery and other processes aimed at separating gold, silver, platinum-group elements and other noble metals for reuse.
[C22B 11/044] from pyrometallurgical residues, e.g. from ashes, dross, flue dust, mud, skim, slag, sludge -- C22B 11/044 concerns the recovery of noble metals from pyrometallurgical waste streams, including ashes, dross, flue dust, mud, skim, slag and sludge. The classification falls under chemistry-metallurgy-production and refining of metals and addresses processes for extracting precious metals from residues generated during high-temperature metal processing.
[C22B 11/046] from manufactured products, e.g. from printed circuit boards, from photographic films, paper or baths -- C22B 11/046 covers methods for recovering noble metals, such as gold, silver or platinum, from waste or scrap manufactured items. It includes processes that extract these metals from products like printed circuit boards, photographic films, paper, or chemical baths used in industrial or laboratory settings. This subclass falls under the chemistry hierarchy for metallurgy and metal production and refining.
[C22B 11/048] from spent catalysts -- The subclass C22B 11/048 covers processes for extracting noble metals by treating spent catalysts that have become loaded with valuable metals during use. It includes chemical or metallurgical steps that recover gold, platinum, palladium and related elements from the catalyst matrix as part of metal production and refining.
[C22B 11/06] Chloridising -- Chloridising (C22B 11/06) is the treatment of metal ores or concentrates with chlorine-containing reagents to produce metal chlorides, a step that enables the extraction and purification of noble metals such as gold, silver or platinum. In hydrometallurgical refining the volatile chlorides are separated and later reduced to obtain the pure metal.
[C22B 11/08] by cyaniding -- C22B 11/08 covers methods for extracting noble metals, such as gold or silver, from ores or concentrates using cyanide solutions. The classification details the chemical treatment steps, solution concentrations, pH control, and subsequent recovery techniques that enable efficient leaching and separation of these valuable metals.
[C22B 1/11] Removing sulfur, phosphorus or arsenic other than by roasting -- C22B 1/11 covers processes for eliminating sulfur, phosphorus or arsenic from ores or scrap without using roasting, such as leaching, hydrometallurgical or electrolytic treatments. It falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Production and refining of metals → Preliminary treatment of ores or scrap.
[C22B 11/10] by amalgamating -- C22B 11/10, under the hierarchy Chemistry → Metallurgy → Production and Refining of Metals, covers methods for obtaining noble metals through amalgamation, where a metal is dissolved or extracted by forming an amalgam with mercury and subsequently recovered. This includes processes that use mercury to separate or purify gold, silver, platinum-group metals or other noble elements.
[C22B 11/12] Apparatus therefor -- This subclass covers equipment used in processes to extract or recover noble metals such as gold, silver or platinum from ores, concentrates, or waste streams. It includes reactors, leaching vessels, electrolysis cells and related handling and filtration devices designed for the production and refining of noble metals.
[C22B 1/14] Agglomerating -- Agglomerating covers methods of binding fine metallic particles, ore fragments or scrap into larger, handleable masses such as briquettes, pellets or sinters before further metallurgical processing. Techniques may employ mechanical pressure, heat, chemical binders or a combination of these to improve transport, storage or subsequent processing efficiency.
[C22B 1/16] Sintering -- Sintering is a preliminary treatment of ores or scrap in which fine metal particles or powders are heated below their melting point until they bond together into a solid mass. The process increases material density and permeability, facilitating subsequent metallurgical operations such as reduction, leaching or melting, and is a key step in the production and refining of metals.
[C22B 1/18] in sinter pots -- C22B 1/18 covers the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap conducted in sinter pots, where the material is heated and agglomerated before further metallurgical processing. It includes methods and apparatus for forming sintered masses in pots to improve subsequent extraction or refining steps.
[C22B 1/20] in sintering machines with movable grates -- This subclass covers the use of sintering machines that incorporate movable grates for the preliminary treatment of metal ores or scrap. The movable grate design enables continuous feeding of raw material and removal of sintered product, enhancing the efficiency of the sintering stage in metal production.
[C22B 1/205] regulation of the sintering process -- C22B 1/205 covers methods and systems for controlling the sintering of metal powders or ore particles, including temperature, atmosphere and feed-rate adjustments to achieve desired density and microstructure. It falls under production and refining of metals, specifically the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap.
[C22B 1/212] in tunnel furnaces -- C22B 1/212 refers to the use of tunnel furnaces for the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap in metal production. A tunnel furnace is a continuous, insulated chamber through which material moves while being heated for drying, sintering, or initial reduction, providing uniform processing before further refining steps.
[C22B 1/214] in shaft furnaces -- C22B 1/214 pertains to the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap carried out in shaft furnaces, which are vertical reactors where material is heated while gases rise through the charge. It includes processes such as roasting, calcination, reduction or sintering performed before further refining steps.
[C22B 1/216] in rotary furnaces -- C22B 1/216 relates to the use of rotary furnaces for the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap in metallurgical processes. It covers heating, drying, calcining, or reduction steps performed in a rotating furnace before further refining. This subclass falls under chemistry - metallurgy - production and refining of metals - preliminary treatment of ores or scrap.
[C22B 1/22] in other sintering apparatus -- C22B 1/22 covers preliminary treatment of ores or scrap by sintering using apparatus other than conventional sintering furnaces, such as rotary kilns, fluidized-bed systems, or other specialized equipment. The subclass addresses the method and equipment employed to agglomerate or preheat material before further metallurgical processing.
[C22B 1/24] Binding -- C22B 1/24 covers processes for binding together ore particles or scrap metal during preliminary treatment, such as adding binders, adhesives or agglomerating agents to improve handling, transport, or subsequent processing. The techniques aim to form coherent lumps or briquettes that facilitate extraction, reduction or refining steps.
[C22B 1/2406] pelletizing -- C22B 1/2406 covers the pelletizing of ores or scrap, a preliminary treatment that agglomerates fine-particle material into small, roughly spherical pellets to improve handling, transport and downstream metallurgical operations such as sintering or reduction. The process typically employs mixing with binders, shaping by rotating drums or presses, and drying or mild heating to create mechanically stable pellets suitable for subsequent metal production.
[C22B 1/2413] enduration of pellets -- The subclass C22B 1/2413 covers methods for endurating metallurgical pellets, i.e., strengthening or hardening them after formation to improve handling, transport and subsequent processing. Techniques may include heat treatment, binding agents, or mechanical compression applied to iron ore, other metal ores or scrap pellets before further refinement.
[C22B 1/242] with binders -- The CPC subclass C22B 1/242 covers preliminary treatment of ores or scrap in which binders are employed, such as agglomeration, pelletising or briquetting processes that aid handling, transport or subsequent metallurgical steps. It falls under chemistry-metallurgy, specifically production and refining of metals.
[C22B 1/243] inorganic -- C22B 1/243 covers the use of inorganic substances in the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap, including chemicals, reagents and fluxes employed to prepare metallic feedstocks before further processing. This sub-group relates to the initial steps of extraction, such as leaching, washing or grinding, where inorganic agents facilitate the removal or separation of valuable metals.
[C22B 1/244] organic -- C22B 1/244 covers the use of organic substances in the preliminary treatment of ores or scrap, such as organic leaching agents, complexing agents, or solvents applied before further metallurgical processing. The entry addresses methods where organic chemicals facilitate ore breakdown, impurity removal, or metal recovery in the early stages of production.
[C22B 1/245] with carbonaceous material for the production of coked agglomerates -- This subclass deals with adding carbonaceous material during the early processing of ores or scrap to create coked agglomerates. The resulting agglomerates improve handling and facilitate downstream metal production steps.

[C22B 1/26] Cooling of roasted, sintered, or agglomerated ores -- This subclass covers processes for cooling ores after high-temperature treatment such as roasting, sintering or agglomeration, typically to ready the material for grinding, handling, or further processing. It includes methods like water quenching, air cooling, forced convection, and other techniques to lower the temperature of ore particles.

[C22B 15/0002] Preliminary treatment -- The code C22B 15/0002 relates to preliminary treatment steps applied to copper ores or concentrates before the main refining processes. It covers operations such as crushing, grinding, leaching, flotation, or other physical-chemical actions that condition the material, remove gangue, or adjust its composition to facilitate subsequent smelting or electrolytic refining.
[C22B 15/0004] without modification of the copper constituent -- C22B 15/0004 covers processes for producing copper in which the metal's chemical composition is left unchanged, meaning the copper is recovered without any alteration of its elemental constituent. [C22B 15/0006] by dry processes -- C22B 15/0006 designates patent filings that describe the production of copper through dry metallurgical methods, excluding aqueous or liquid-phase techniques. [C22B 15/001] with modification of the copper constituent -- C22B 15/001 pertains to methods for producing copper in which the copper element is deliberately altered, such as by alloying, doping, or chemical modification, during the extraction or refining stages. [C22B 15/0041] in converters -- C22B 15/0041 covers copper production steps carried out in converter furnaces, where copper matte or other intermediate is oxidized, reduced and refined to produce metallic copper. [C22B 15/0043] in rotating converters -- C22B 15/0043 covers methods for producing copper in rotating converters, where molten copper feedstock undergoes oxidation-reduction reactions while the vessel rotates to enhance mixing and heat transfer. [C22B 15/0045] in muffles, crucibles, or closed vessels -- C22B 15/0045 designates copper-obtaining processes that are performed in muffles, crucibles or other closed vessels, emphasizing the heating, melting or reduction steps carried out within sealed containers. [C22B 15/0047] flash smelting or converting -- C22B 15/0047 covers flash smelting and converting processes used to obtain copper from its ores. [C22B 15/005] in a succession of furnaces -- C22B 15/005 covers processes for obtaining copper that employ a series of furnaces arranged in succession, where the metal passes through multiple heating stages to achieve refining or alloying. [C22B 15/0052] Reduction smelting or converting -- C22B 15/0052 covers processes that convert copper ores or concentrates into metallic copper by reduction smelting or converting, where the metal is extracted through high-temperature chemical reactions with a reducing agent. [C22B 15/0054] Slag, slime, speiss, or dross treating -- The CPC entry C22B 15/0054 covers processes for treating metallurgical residues such as slag, slime, speiss or dross generated in copper production. It includes methods for recovering valuable metals, removing impurities and preparing the waste for disposal or reuse, typically through physical, chemical or thermal treatments. [C22B 15/0056] Scrap treating -- C22B 15/0056 relates to processes for treating scrap metal in order to recover copper, encompassing mechanical, chemical or electrolytic methods that remove impurities and prepare the material for subsequent refining steps.
[C22B 15/0058] Spent catalysts -- The CPC subclass C22B 15/0058 covers the handling, treatment and disposal of spent catalysts used in copper production and refining processes. It includes methods for recovering valuable metals from exhausted catalytic materials, regenerating catalysts, and managing waste to minimise environmental impact.
[C22B 15/006] working up of molten copper, e.g. refining -- The subgroup C22B 15/006 covers techniques for processing molten copper after it has been melted, focusing on refining steps that remove impurities, adjust composition, and improve metal quality. Methods include fire or electrolytic refining, slagging, casting adjustments, and other treatments applied to the liquid metal before solidification.
[C22B 15/0063] Hydrometallurgy -- C22B 15/0063 relates to hydrometallurgical methods for extracting copper from ores or concentrates, including leaching with aqueous solutions, solvent extraction, precipitation, and electrowinning. The code covers processes that use chemical reactions in liquid phase to separate and purify copper, often as part of refining operations. It falls under production and refining of metals within the chemistry and metallurgy hierarchy.
[C22B 15/0065] Leaching or slurrying  with organic compounds  C22B3/16
[C22B 15/0067] with acids or salts thereof -- The subclass C22B 15/0067 covers copper extraction methods that employ acids or acid-derived salts, such as leaching, solvent-extraction or other chemical treatments using acidic media to dissolve or recover copper from ores or concentrates. It is part of the broader metallurgical processes for producing and refining copper.
[C22B 15/0069] containing halogen -- The C22B 15/0069 subclass covers methods for obtaining copper in which the metal or its intermediate compounds contain a halogen element. It pertains to metallurgical processes that involve halogen-containing feedstocks, alloys, or reagents during copper production or refining.
[C22B 15/0071] containing sulfur -- C22B 15/0071 covers methods for obtaining copper in which sulfur is present, either as a reactant, additive or impurity during the refining process. It includes sulfur-based smelting, leaching and other metallurgical steps where sulfur influences copper recovery.
[C22B 15/0073] containing nitrogen -- This CPC subgroup concerns copper that contains nitrogen, covering alloys, treatments or refining processes in which nitrogen is intentionally introduced into copper to modify its properties, such as hardness, strength or corrosion resistance. It includes the preparation of nitrogen-bearing copper materials and related technical details.
[C22B 15/0076] Cyanide groups -- The subclass C22B 15/0076 covers the use of cyanide compounds in the extraction and recovery of copper, including cyanide leaching, precipitation and other processes that employ cyanide groups to obtain copper from ores or concentrates. It falls under Chemistry → Metallurgy → Production and refining of metals → Obtaining copper.
[C22B 15/0078] with ammoniacal solutions, e.g. ammonium hydroxide -- This CPC subclass deals with processes for obtaining copper that employ ammoniacal solutions, for example ammonium hydroxide, as the leaching or recovery medium. It covers techniques where the copper is extracted, dissolved, or refined using such alkaline nitrogen-containing liquids.
[C22B 15/008] with non-acid solutions containing salts of alkali or alkaline earth metals -- C22B 15/008 covers processes for extracting copper that employ non-acidic liquids in which alkali-metal or alkaline-earth-metal salts are dissolved, such as ammonia-based or carbonate solutions. These methods avoid acidic media, often improving metal selectivity and reducing corrosion during the refining stage.
[C22B 15/0082] with water -- This CPC subclass describes processes for obtaining copper by using water as a solvent or reactant, typically in hydrometallurgical operations such as leaching, solvent extraction and aqueous refining. It covers aqueous leach baths, pressure leaching and related steps.
[C22B 15/0084] Treating solutions  with organic compounds  C22B3/20 -- The subclass concerns processes used in copper production that employ organic reagents to treat aqueous solutions, such as leaching, solvent-extraction, precipitation or other chemical steps that isolate or refine copper from its solution phase. It includes the selection, application and control of organic compounds that facilitate copper recovery or purification.
[C22B 15/0086] by physical methods -- The CPC subclass C22B 15/0086 covers physical techniques employed to obtain copper, including electrolytic refining, electro-extraction, and pyrometallurgical operations such as smelting or casting that separate copper from ores or intermediates without chemical reagents. This falls under production and refining of metals.
[C22B 15/0089] by chemical methods -- C22B 15/0089 covers chemical techniques for producing copper, including leaching, solvent-extraction, precipitation and electrolytic processes used to extract copper from ores, concentrates or secondary sources. It addresses the preparation of copper metal or compounds by reacting the material with reagents, followed by purification steps.
[C22B 15/0091] by cementation -- C22B 15/0091 relates to the production of copper by cementation, a hydrometallurgical technique where copper ions in solution are reduced and deposited on a more reactive metal such as iron or zinc. The process exploits the difference in electrode potentials to precipitate metallic copper, and it is used for recovery from leachates, residues or waste streams. This subclass falls under the broader field of metallurgy and metal refining.
[C22B 15/0093] by gases, e.g. hydrogen or hydrogen sulfide -- The subclass C22B 15/0093 concerns methods for extracting copper by employing gaseous agents such as hydrogen or hydrogen sulfide as reducers. It falls under the metallurgy section dealing with the production and refining of metals, specifically the chemical processes used to obtain copper from its ores or concentrates.
[C22B 15/0095] Process control or regulation methods -- The CPC subclass C22B 15/0095 covers techniques for controlling or regulating the copper-production process, including monitoring parameters, adjusting operating conditions, and applying feedback or automation to ensure efficient extraction and refining of copper. It falls within the broader categories of chemistry, metallurgy and metal production.
[C22B 15/0097] Sulfur release abatement -- C22B 15/0097 pertains to techniques used in the copper production process to control or reduce the release of sulfur compounds. It covers abatement methods such as gas treatment, sulfur capture, and process modifications that limit sulfur emissions during smelting, refining, or related metallurgical operations.
[C22B 17/00] Obtaining cadmium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  The extraction metallurgy of cadmium including refining ( C22B17/02 - C22B17/06 ).
[C22B 17/02] by dry processes -- C22B 17/02 covers processes for producing cadmium by dry methods, such as roasting cadmium-containing ores, reducing solid compounds, or extracting cadmium in the vapor phase, without using aqueous solutions. These techniques are employed in metallurgy to isolate cadmium from its concentrates or intermediates.
[C22B 17/04] by wet processes -- C22B 17/04 covers the extraction of cadmium by wet methods, encompassing hydrometallurgical techniques such as leaching, precipitation, solvent extraction and electrowinning. The subclass deals with processes that dissolve cadmium-containing ores or alloys in aqueous solutions and recover the metal in a purified form.
[C22B 17/06] Refining -- The subclass C22B 17/06 concerns methods for refining cadmium, including the extraction of the metal from ores, concentrates or secondary sources and the removal of impurities. It covers chemical, electrolytic, thermal and other processes used to produce high-purity cadmium suitable for industrial applications.
[C22B 19/00] Obtaining zinc or zinc oxide -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Preliminary treatment of zinc ores as well as preliminary refining of zinc oxide ( C22B19/02 ).  Obtaining zinc by distilling ( C22B19/04 - C22B19/18 ).  Obtaining zinc other than by distilling ( C22B19/20 - C22B19/26 ).  Obtaining zinc from residues ( C22B19/28 and C22B19/30 ).  Refining zinc ( C22B19/32 ).  Obtaining zinc oxide ( C22B19/34 - C22B19/38 ).  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Zinc oxide obtained by non-metallurgical process -> C01G9/02
[C22B 19/02] Preliminary treatment of ores -- C22B 19/02 covers the preliminary processing steps applied to zinc-bearing ores before the extraction of metallic zinc or the production of zinc oxide. It includes crushing, grinding, sizing, and other mechanical or physical treatments that prepare the ore for subsequent leaching, roasting or smelting operations.
[C22B 19/04] Obtaining zinc by distilling -- C22B 19/04 covers methods for producing zinc by distillation, including the recovery of zinc or zinc oxide from metallic or compound sources through vapor-phase separation. The subclass falls under chemistry-metallurgy-production and refining of metals and specifies distillation-based techniques for isolating zinc in a purified form.
[C22B 19/06] in muffle furnaces -- C22B 19/06 covers methods for obtaining zinc or zinc oxide that employ muffle furnaces, sealed high-temperature reactors in which the metal or oxide is heated in a controlled atmosphere to facilitate reduction, oxidation or purification. This subclass falls under the chemistry-metallurgy hierarchy for production and refining of metals.
[C22B 19/08] in blast furnaces -- C22B 19/08 concerns the production of zinc or zinc oxide by means of blast furnaces. It includes the reduction of zinc-containing ores, the treatment of furnace slag and the collection of metallic zinc or its oxide during the smelting process.
[C22B 19/10] in reverberatory furnaces -- The C22B 19/10 subclass covers methods for producing zinc or zinc oxide that employ reverberatory furnaces, where heat is reflected off a roof or ceiling onto the charge. It includes the specific arrangements, temperature controls, and feedstock handling used in these furnace-based reduction or oxidation processes.
[C22B 19/12] in crucible furnaces -- The C22B 19/12 subclass covers processes for producing zinc or zinc oxide that are carried out in crucible furnaces. It deals with the metallurgical steps of heating, melting or reducing zinc-containing materials within a sealed or open crucible to obtain the metal or its oxide. This falls under chemistry-metallurgy methods for metal production and refining.
[C22B 19/14] in vertical retorts -- C22B 19/14 covers the production of zinc or zinc oxide using vertical retorts, where the material is charged into an upright vessel and heated to effect reduction or oxidation. The classification applies to processes that employ this specific retort geometry for refining or obtaining the metal or its oxide.
[C22B 19/16] Distilling vessels -- The C22B 19/16 subclass covers distilling vessels used in the production or refining of zinc and zinc oxide. It includes the design, construction and operation of equipment where zinc-containing vapours are condensed to recover metal or oxide, encompassing reactors, condensers, and related ancillary parts within metallurgical processing plants.
[C22B 19/18] Condensers, Receiving vessels -- The C22B 19/18 class covers condensers and receiving vessels employed in zinc or zinc-oxide production. It includes equipment that cools zinc vapor and collects the condensed metal or oxide, as well as the design and operation of these units within the refining process.
[C22B 19/20] Obtaining zinc otherwise than by distilling -- C22B 19/20 covers methods for producing zinc or zinc oxide that do not involve distillation, including electrolytic reduction, hydrometallurgical leaching, and direct reduction of zinc-containing ores or intermediates. The subclass falls under chemistry, metallurgy and production and refining of metals, focusing on alternative zinc extraction routes.
[C22B 19/22] with leaching with acids -- C22B 19/22 covers the production of zinc or zinc oxide by leaching zinc-bearing materials with mineral acids. The subclass details acid-based dissolution steps used to extract zinc from ores or scrap before precipitation or electrowinning, fitting within the metallurgy hierarchy of metal production and refining.
[C22B 19/24] with leaching with alkaline solutions, e.g. ammonia -- C22B 19/24 covers processes for extracting zinc or zinc oxide by leaching ores or concentrates with alkaline reagents such as ammonia. The method involves treating the material in an alkaline solution to dissolve zinc compounds, which are then recovered.
[C22B 19/26] Refining solutions containing zinc values, e.g. obtained by leaching zinc ores  treatment or purification of solutions by liquid-liquid extraction, by ion exchange or by adsorption  C22B3/00 -- C22B 19/26 covers processes for refining aqueous solutions that contain zinc extracted from leached zinc ores. It includes methods such as liquid-liquid extraction, ion exchange and adsorption to purify the zinc value before further metallurgical processing.
[C22B 19/28] from muffle furnace residues -- C22B 19/28 covers processes for recovering zinc or zinc oxide from the solid residues left after muffle furnace operations. It includes chemical or metallurgical steps that extract the metal or its oxide from furnace slags, ash or other byproducts.
[C22B 19/30] from metallic residues or scraps -- C22B 19/30 covers processes for producing zinc or zinc oxide by recovering the metal from metallic residues, scraps or other secondary sources, including recycling of zinc-containing waste streams within the broader context of metal production and refining.
[C22B 19/32] Refining zinc -- C22B 19/32 covers the industrial processes used to obtain and refine metallic zinc or zinc oxide, including the separation of zinc from its ores, the removal of impurities, and methods such as electrolytic, thermal or chemical reduction employed to produce pure zinc metal or its oxide.
[C22B 19/34] Obtaining zinc oxide -- C22B 19/34 covers industrial processes for producing zinc oxide from zinc-containing feedstocks, including oxidation, roasting, leaching and precipitation steps that convert metallic zinc or zinc compounds into ZnO. The entry details chemical and thermal methods used to isolate the oxide in bulk form for use in ceramics, rubber, pigments and other applications.
[C22B 19/36] in blast or reverberatory furnaces -- This CPC subclass covers the production of zinc or zinc oxide using blast or reverberatory furnaces, describing metallurgical processes where zinc ores are reduced or oxidized in these high-temperature furnace types. It falls under chemistry, metallurgy, and metal production and refining.
[C22B 19/38] in rotary furnaces -- The C22B 19/38 subclass covers processes for producing zinc or zinc oxide that are carried out in rotary-furnace reactors, including the furnace construction, heating technique, raw-material feeding and product recovery specific to this type of continuous, rotating furnace system.

[C22B 23/00] Obtaining nickel or cobalt -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Preliminary treatment of ores ( C22B15/0002 ).  By dry processes ( C22B23/02 - C22B23/028 ).  By wet processes ( C22B23/04 - C22B11/048 ).  Refining ( C22B23/06 and C22B23/065 ).
[C22B 23/005] Preliminary treatment of ores, e.g. by roasting or by the Krupp-Renn process -- C22B 23/005 relates to the early processing of ores, specifically methods like roasting or the Krupp-Renn technique, used to prepare nickel or cobalt for further extraction. [C22B 23/02] by dry processes -- C22B 23/02 covers dry metallurgical methods for obtaining nickel or cobalt, such as roasting, calcination, reduction or other processes carried out without liquid media. It pertains to the production and refining of these metals where heat or gas-phase reactions are applied, distinguishing these techniques from wet leaching or electrolytic routes.
[C22B 23/021] by reduction in solid state, e.g. by segregation processes -- C22B 23/021 covers processes for obtaining nickel or cobalt by reducing the metal in the solid state, for example through segregation or other solid-state reduction techniques. These methods avoid melting and typically involve heating or chemical treatment that causes the metal to separate from its ore or precursor within the solid matrix.

The classification applies to processes that transform raw antimony compounds into refined, commercially usable antimony metal.
[C22B 30/04] Obtaining arsenic -- C22B 30/04 covers the extraction and purification of arsenic from its ores or by-product streams, including leaching, roasting, sublimation and other chemical or physical steps used to isolate arsenic in elemental or compound form for industrial use. It falls under the metallurgical pathway for producing and refining antimony, arsenic or bismuth.
[C22B 30/06] Obtaining bismuth -- This CPC subclass C22B 30/06 covers processes for extracting bismuth from ores or concentrates, including chemical and physical methods used in the production and refining of bismuth within the broader field of metallurgy.
[C22B 3/02] Apparatus therefor -- This subclass covers equipment used in wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates, such as reactors, leaching tanks, solvent-extraction columns, precipitation vessels and related piping, agitators and control devices designed for hydrometallurgical processing.
[C22B 3/04] by leaching -- C22B 3/04 refers to the leaching stage of metal extraction, where metal compounds are dissolved from ores or concentrates using aqueous solutions in wet chemical processes. It covers methods such as acid, alkaline, or cyanide leaching that separate the desired metal for subsequent recovery and refining. This subclass falls under the broader hierarchy of chemistry, metallurgy, and production and refining of metals.
[C22B 3/045] Leaching using electrochemical processes -- Electrochemical leaching employs an electric current to promote the dissolution of metal compounds from ores or concentrates in a wet medium, often using acidic or alkaline electrolytes. The process converts insoluble minerals into soluble ions, enabling subsequent recovery and purification of the target metal. It is applied in the extraction of metals such as copper, uranium and nickel where conventional chemical leaching is less efficient.
[C22B 3/06] in inorganic acid solutions -- C22B 3/06 covers wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates by leaching in inorganic acid solutions, such as sulfuric, nitric or hydrochloric acid, to dissolve the desired metal for subsequent recovery.
[C22B 3/065] Nitric acids or salts thereof -- This CPC subclass covers the use of nitric acid and its salts in wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates, including leaching, dissolution and related chemical treatments within metallurgical refining processes.
[C22B 3/08] Sulfuric acid -- C22B 3/08 addresses the use of sulfuric acid in wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It includes processes where sulfuric acid serves as a leaching or dissolution medium to recover metals, as well as related steps such as acid regeneration, purification and treatment of spent solutions.
[C22B 3/10] Hydrochloric acid -- C22B 3/10 refers to the application of hydrochloric acid in wet extraction processes for recovering metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It includes leaching, dissolution and related steps where HCl is used to separate metals during production and refining.
[C22B 3/12] in inorganic alkaline solutions -- C22B 3/12 covers the use of inorganic alkaline solutions, such as sodium or potassium hydroxide, for the wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It includes processes where the alkaline medium dissolves or leaches metals, facilitating their separation and recovery in metallurgical production. This sub-class falls under the broader category of wet extraction methods in the production and refining of metals.
[C22B 3/14] containing ammonia or ammonium salts -- C22B 3/14 covers wet leaching processes in which ammonia or ammonium salts are employed as reagents to extract metal compounds from ores or concentrates. The classification includes the preparation of ammoniacal solutions, the dissolution of metal sulfides, oxides or carbonates, and subsequent precipitation or recovery steps that rely on the presence of ammonia or its salts.
[C22B 3/16] in organic solutions -- The subclass C22B 3/16 covers wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates when the leaching medium is an organic solution. It includes processes that dissolve metals in organic solvents rather than aqueous media, often to improve selectivity, reduce corrosion, or recover metals from low-grade feeds. This falls under the broader domain of metallurgy and the production and refining of metals.
[C22B 3/1608] Leaching with acyclic or carbocyclic agents -- The subclass C22B 3/1608 covers wet leaching processes that employ acyclic or carbocyclic organic compounds as reagents to dissolve metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It includes the selection, formulation and use of these agents for extracting metals in metallurgical refining.
[C22B 3/1616] Leaching with acyclic or carbocyclic agents of a single type -- C22B 3/1616 covers wet leaching processes in which metal compounds are extracted from ores or concentrates using a single acyclic or carbocyclic leaching agent. The method relies on one type of organic molecule-such as a linear acid, an alcohol, or a carbocyclic compound-to dissolve the target metal without employing mixtures or additional reagents.
[C22B 3/1625] with amines  amino acids  C22B3/165
[C22B 3/1633] with oximes -- C22B 3/1633 covers wet-process extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates where oximes are employed as complexing agents or precipitants. The method uses oxime ligands to selectively bind metal ions in solution, facilitating their separation and recovery during hydrometallurgical refining.
[C22B 3/1641] with ketones or aldehydes -- This CPC subclass covers wet extraction methods for metal compounds from ores or concentrates in which ketones or aldehydes are employed as reagents or solvents, typically to leach or dissolve the target metal during the refining stage. It falls under metallurgy, production and refining of metals, and the extraction of metal compounds by wet processes.
[C22B 3/165] with organic acids -- This subclass covers wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates where organic acids are employed as leaching agents, forming soluble metal-acid complexes that can be separated and recovered. It pertains to processes that use acids such as citric, oxalic or acetic acid to dissolve target metals in the production and refining of metals.
[C22B 3/1658] Leaching with acyclic or carbocyclic agents of different types in admixture, e.g. with organic acids added to oximes -- The CPC subclass C22B 3/1658 covers wet leaching methods in metallurgy that employ mixtures of acyclic or carbocyclic agents, for example combining organic acids with oximes, to extract metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It relates to combined-agent leaching processes used in metal production and refining.
[C22B 3/1666] Leaching with heterocyclic compounds -- C22B 3/1666 pertains to wet leaching processes that employ heterocyclic compounds to dissolve metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It falls within the chemistry-metallurgy hierarchy, under production and refining of metals, specifically the extraction of metals by wet methods.
[C22B 3/1675] Leaching with a mixture of organic agents wherein one agent at least is a heterocyclic compounds  C22B3/1683  takes precedence -- Leaching of metal compounds from ores or concentrates by wet processes using a mixture of organic agents, where at least one of the agents is a heterocyclic compound, is covered by CPC code C22B 3/1675. This subclass is superseded by the more specific C22B 3/1683.
[C22B 3/1683] Leaching with organo-metallic compounds -- C22B 3/1683 covers wet leaching processes that use organo-metallic compounds to dissolve metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It addresses the selection, preparation and application of such organometallic reagents for metal extraction and recovery, situated within the broader fields of chemistry, metallurgy and metal production.
[C22B 3/1691] Leaching with a mixture of organic agents wherein at least one agent is an organo-metallic compound -- The code C22B 3/1691 covers wet extraction methods in which metal compounds are leached using a blend of organic reagents, with at least one reagent being an organometallic compound. This approach is used to dissolve ores or concentrates in order to separate the target metal.
[C22B 3/18] with the aid of microorganisms or enzymes, e.g. bacteria or algae -- This subclass covers wet extraction techniques in which microorganisms or enzymes, such as bacteria or algae, are used to leach or solubilise metal compounds from ores or concentrates, enabling metal recovery through biologically assisted processes.
[C22B 3/20] Treatment or purification of solutions, e.g. obtained by leaching -- This subclass covers methods for treating or purifying aqueous solutions obtained by leaching ores or concentrates, emphasizing processes that remove impurities, adjust composition, or recover valuable metals before subsequent refining. It is positioned within wet extraction of metal compounds in the metallurgy hierarchy.
[C22B 3/205] using adducts or inclusion complexes -- The class covers wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates in which adducts or inclusion complexes are employed to solubilise, complex or otherwise assist the separation of the target metal. It includes processes that form or use such complexes to improve leaching, precipitation or purification steps in metallurgical production.
[C22B 3/22] by physical processes, e.g. by filtration, by magnetic means  -- C22B 3/22 covers physical methods used to extract metal compounds from ores or concentrates, such as filtration or magnetic separation, within the broader metallurgical domain of wet extraction processes. This subclass is part of the CPC hierarchy under chemistry, metallurgy, and production and refining of metals.
[C22B 3/24] by adsorption on solid substances, e.g. by extraction with solid resins -- C22B 3/24 relates to wet-process extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates where the metal is recovered by adsorption onto solid materials, such as using ion-exchange or extraction resins. This technique separates the desired metal by binding it to a solid phase rather than by precipitation or solvent extraction.
[C22B 3/26] by liquid-liquid extraction using organic compounds -- In groups C22B3/262 - C22B3/41 : the last place priority rule is applied, i.e. at each hierarchical level, in the absence of an indication to the contrary, compounds are classified in the last appropriate place; when two or more compounds are used successively, each compound is classified as such; mixtures containing two or more compounds covered individually by the same one of groups C22B3/262 - C22B3/387 , are classified only in that group.
[C22B 3/262] using alcohols or phenols -- C22B 3/262 covers wet metallurgical processes that recover metal compounds from ores or concentrates by using alcohols or phenols as leaching agents, specifying solvent-based extraction methods within the broader production and refining of metals.
[C22B 3/28] Amines -- The CPC subclass C22B 3/28 covers the use of amines in wet extraction processes for recovering metals from ores or concentrates. It includes amines employed as reagents, extractants or complexing agents that facilitate leaching, solvent extraction or other aqueous treatments within the broader field of metallurgy and metal production.
[C22B 3/282] Aliphatic amines -- The CPC entry C22B 3/282 covers the use of aliphatic amines in wet extraction processes for recovering metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It includes methods where primary, secondary or tertiary aliphatic amines act as leaching agents, complexing or stabilising reagents during metallurgical wet-treatment.
[C22B 3/284] Aromatic amines -- C22B 3/284 covers the use of aromatic amines as reagents in wet-process extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It includes methods where such amines form soluble complexes or aid leaching to recover metals, and pertains to the chemistry of metallurgical refining that employs these organic nitrogen compounds.
[C22B 3/286] Amino-alcohols -- The subclass C22B 3/286 deals with amino-alcohols employed in wet extraction processes for recovering metals from ores or concentrates. These compounds function as complexing agents, leaching solvents or precipitants that bind metal ions and facilitate their dissolution or separation. The classification covers both individual amino-alcohols and mixtures used in hydrometallurgical operations.
[C22B 3/288] Quaternary ammonium -- C22B 3/288 pertains to the use of quaternary ammonium compounds in the wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It covers methods in which these surfactants act as reagents, collectors or extractants to leach, separate or purify metals during hydrometallurgical processing.
[C22B 3/30] Oximes -- Oximes are organic compounds containing a carbon-nitrogen-oxygen functional group (C=NOH) that can form stable complexes with metal ions. In wet extraction they are used as reagents or extractants to solubilise and separate metal compounds from ores or concentrates, often in hydrometallurgical processes.
[C22B 3/302] Ethers or epoxides -- This subclass covers the use of organic ethers or epoxy compounds as solvents or extractants in wet metallurgical processes for separating metal compounds from ores or concentrates, including their role in leaching, solvent-extraction, liquid-liquid extraction and related purification steps.
[C22B 3/304] Crown ethers -- C22B 3/304 covers the use of crown ethers - cyclic polyethers that selectively bind metal ions - in wet extraction processes for separating metals from ores or concentrates. The subclass includes methods, reagents and apparatus that employ these macrocyclic ligands to improve leaching, solvent extraction or ion-exchange steps in metallurgy.
[C22B 3/306] Ketones or aldehydes -- C22B 3/306 covers wet extraction processes for metal compounds from ores or concentrates in which ketones or aldehydes are used as extracting agents, solvents or reagents. The subclass resides under chemistry → metallurgy → production and refining of metals → extraction of metal compounds by wet processes, and defines methods that employ these carbonyl compounds to leach, separate or purify metals.
[C22B 3/32] Carboxylic acids -- C22B 3/32 covers the use of carboxylic acids in wet extraction processes for producing metals from ores or concentrates. It includes leaching, solvent extraction and related steps where organic acids act as reagents to dissolve metal compounds, enabling subsequent purification or refining.
[C22B 3/322] Oxalic acids -- C22B 3/322 concerns the application of oxalic acids in wet leaching operations to dissolve metal compounds from ores or concentrates during metallurgical extraction. It includes processes that use oxalic acid solutions to solubilise and recover metals such as iron, copper or rare earth elements, focusing on the chemistry of the acid-metal interaction and subsequent purification steps.
[C22B 3/324] Naphthenic acids -- C22B 3/324 covers the use of naphthenic acids in wet extraction processes for recovering metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It includes methods where these organic acids act as leaching or solvent-extraction agents to dissolve metals such as copper, nickel or zinc. The classification applies to techniques that employ naphthenic acid solutions to improve metal recovery efficiency.

[C22B 3/34] containing sulfur -- C22B 3/34 addresses wet extraction techniques for metal compounds from ores or concentrates that involve sulfur. The subclass includes leaching, dissolution, or precipitation processes where sulfide or sulfate reagents are used to liberate and recover metals.
[C22B 3/36] Heterocyclic compounds -- C22B 3/36 covers heterocyclic compounds employed in the wet extraction of metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It pertains to chemical methods used in metallurgy for the production and refining of metals, specifically those that involve aqueous or other liquid-phase processes to isolate metal-bearing substances. The classification captures inventions that use ring-structured organic molecules to improve leaching, solubilisation or precipitation of target metals.
[C22B 3/362] Heterocyclic compounds of a single type -- This subclass covers wet-metal extraction processes that use heterocyclic organic reagents containing a single type of hetero-atom (e.g., only nitrogen, oxygen or sulphur) as leaching or complexing agents. It includes the preparation, application, and recovery of such single-type heterocycles in the dissolution of metal ores or concentrates.
[C22B 3/364] Quinoline -- C22B 3/364 designates the use of quinoline, an aromatic heterocyclic solvent, in wet extraction or leaching operations for recovering metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It falls under the metallurgy section that addresses production and refining of metals through aqueous processing methods.
[C22B 3/37] containing boron, silicon, selenium or tellurium -- C22B 3/37 covers wet extraction processes for metal compounds that incorporate boron, silicon, selenium or tellurium, detailing how these elements are removed from ores or concentrates during the production and refining of metals.
[C22B 3/38] containing phosphorus -- C22B 3/38 covers wet extraction processes for metal compounds in which phosphorus is present, such as leaching or dissolution steps used to recover metals from ores or concentrates. The classification falls under chemistry->metallurgy->production and refining of metals, focusing on the treatment of phosphorus-containing feedstocks.
[C22B 3/381] Phosphines, e.g. compounds with the formula PR n H 3-n , with n = 0-3 -- The subclass C22B 3/381 covers phosphine compounds of the general formula PR n H 3-n (where n = 0-3), including their preparation, properties and use in wet-process extraction or refining of metal compounds from ores or concentrates. It focuses on applications of these phosphorus-hydrogen-organic species within metallurgical processes.
[C22B 3/382] Phosphine chalcogenides, e.g. compounds of the formula R 3 P=X with X = O, S, Se or Te -- C22B 3/382 covers phosphine chalcogenides, namely compounds of the type R₃P=X where X is oxygen, sulfur, selenium or tellurium, used as reagents in wet-chemical extraction and refining of metals. The entry defines their structure and applications within metallurgical processes for separating metal compounds from ores or concentrates.
[C22B 3/383] Tervalent phosphorus oxyacids, esters thereof -- The C22B 3/383 subclass encompasses tervalent phosphorus oxyacids and their ester derivatives, which are employed as reagents or intermediates in wet-chemical extraction of metal compounds during metallurgical refining.

[C22C] ALLOYS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Ferrous and non ferrous alloys, radioactive alloys, amorphous alloys, alloys containing fibres or filaments.  It covers also cermets, master alloys, metal matrix composites, methods of making amorphous alloys as well as methods of making alloys by melting, by powder metallurgy, by removing material from alloys to produce alloys of different constitution.  Therefore, the term "alloys" includes:  a) metallic composite materials containing a substantial proportion of fibres or other somewhat larger particles;  b) ceramic compositions containing free metal bonded to carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides or silicides, e.g. cermets, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides, other than as macroscopic reinforcing agents.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Working metallic powder, powder metallurgical apparatus or processes -> B22F - Alloys based on non-metals (such as B, Si, Se, Te- based alloys etc.) -> C01B , C01D , C01G - Ceramics -> C04B - Changing the physical structure of ferrous alloys -> C21D - Changing the physical structure of non ferrous metals/alloys -> C22F1/00  **Glossary:** - Alloy: A composition of plural elements at least one of which is a free metal. It also includes material containing any combination of fibres, filaments, whiskers and particles, e.g. carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides, silicides, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides embedded in a metallic matrix - Base / Based on: at least 50% by weight of the specified constituent or of the specified group of constituents, or the metallic element which is the largest constituent of the alloy. - Amorphous: Possessing no regular crystalline arrangement of atoms. - Cermet: Material containing any combination of fibres, filaments, whiskers and particles, e.g. carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides, silicides, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides embedded in a metallic matrix. - Master alloy: A mixture or alloy of elements which are to be added to a charge or molten metal in order to provide a desired composition, deoxidize the molten metal or provide a fine grain size etc. - Refining: Purification of metal by removing impurities therefrom.
[C22C 1/00] Non-ferrous alloys, i.e. alloys based essentially on metals other than iron -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods for making non-ferrous alloys.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Making non-ferrous alloys by electrothermic methods -> C22B4/00 - Making non-ferrous alloys by electrolysis -> C25C1/24 , C25C3/36  **Glossary:** - In situ formation: The phase formed (whether metal or non-metal) is not added in advance, but is generated in situ in the matrix by reaction during the entire process of preparing the alloy, including powder treatment, sintering, etc. - Reaction sintering: The powder raw material undergoes a chemical reaction at a certain temperature and simultaneously performs densification and synthesis of the specified components to obtain a predetermined sintered body.

[C22F] CHANGING THE PHYSICAL STRUCTURE OF NON-FERROUS METALS AND NON-FERROUS ALLOYS -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Changing the physical (metallurgical) structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working;  Changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by special physical methods, e.g. treatment with neutrons.  The term "non-ferrous alloys" refers to alloys based essentially on metals other than iron.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Working metallic powder, powder metallurgical apparatus or processes -> B22F , C22C1/04 - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00 - Electrolytic production or refining of metals -> C25C - Single crystals or homogeneous polycrystalline material with defined structure; production thereof -> C30B  **Glossary:** - Alloy: A composition of plural elements at least one of which is a free metal. It also includes material containing any combination of fibres, filaments, whiskers and particles, e.g. carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides, silicides, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides embedded in a metallic matrix - Recrystallization: After all metal crystals have been dissolved by heating enough to lose its structural strength, the metal temperature then falls, allowing the crystals to re-form - Aging (or ageing): A process in which the hardness or strength of a metal alloy having a constituent in supersaturated solid solution is increased over time as the constituent precipitates out as a secondary phase containing the constituent. When occurring at room temperature the process is termed "natural aging", while a process that occurs when subjecting the metal alloy to elevated temperature is termed "artificial aging". Aging for a longer time than that corresponding to maximum strength or hardness at the particular temperature is termed "over-ageing". - Hardening: The increase in resistance to deformation - Precipitation hardening: As the quenched alloy ages, a new material precipitates out of the metallic crystal lattice, filling in abutting spaces, and increasing hardness - Normalizing: A process of heating metallic material above its critical temperature and cooling in air thereby establishing a fine uniform grain size and improving the microstructural uniformity - Quenching: The rapid cooling of metallic material either from elevated temperature to room temperature or cooling of metal to sub-ambient temperature, at a specific rate, with a given medium. - Tempering: Heating of a previously quenched or normalized metallic material to an elevated temperature, and then cooling under suitable conditions to obtain the desired mechanical properties.
[C22F 1/00] Changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods of changing the physical structure of non-ferrous metals or alloys by heat treatment or by hot or cold working which are not covered in any of B22F , B21B , B21J , C21D , C25C .  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Methods of making alloys by powder metallurgy -> B22F - Heat treatment, e.g. annealing, quenching, tempering, adapted for particular metallic articles; furnaces therefor -> C21D9/00  **Glossary:** - SMA alloys (shape memory alloys): alloys having the ability when originally shaped at a first temperature and reshaped at a second temperature to undergo a reversible thermoelastic transition and resume its original shape when returned to the first temperature or an intermediate temperature - Quenching: Cooling of metallic material at a specific rate, with a given medium.

[C23] COATING METALLIC MATERIAL
[C23C] COATING METALLIC MATERIAL -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Hot-dipping or immersion processes and apparatus for applying the coating material in the molten state without affecting the shape.  Coating by spraying, casting, by vacuum evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation and the different aspects of chemical coating which includes  Chemical coating by decomposition of either gaseous compounds, liquid or solid compounds, solutions or suspensions of the coating forming compounds, without leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating.  Coating starting from inorganic powder.  Coating with metallic material characterized only by the composition of the metallic material.  Chemical surface treatment of metallic materials, leaving reaction products of surface material in the coating.  All coatings referred to in this subclass are either "for metallic materials" or "by metallic material," with the exception of PVD (by vacuum evaporation, by sputtering or by ion implantation), and CVD (an aspect included in "the different aspects of chemical coating").  Solid state diffusion into metallic material surfaces.  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Making metal-coated products by extrusion -> B21C23/22 - Covering with metal by connecting pre-existing layers to articles -> B21D39/00 , B23K - Metallizing of glass -> C03C - Metallizing mortars, concrete, artificial stone, ceramics or natural stone -> C04B41/00 - Enameling of, or applying a vitreous layer to, metals -> C23D - Treating metal surfaces or coating of metals by electrolysis or electrophoresis -> C25D - Single-crystal film growth -> C30B - Metallizing textiles -> D06M11/83 - Decorating textiles by locally metallizing -> D06Q1/04  **Glossary:** - Metallic Material: covers: Metals; Alloys which are metallic composite materials containing a substantial proportion of fibers or other somewhat larger particles; ceramic compositions containing free metal bonded to carbides, diamond, oxides, borides, nitrides or silicides, e.g. cermets, or other metal compounds, e.g. oxynitrides or sulfides, other than as macroscopic reinforcing agents.

[C23C 18/18] Pretreatment of the material to be coated -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pretreatment not specific to a particular substrate as well as pretreatment of metallic substrate to be coated.  **Glossary:** - Sensitising in C23C18/28 and lower: pre-treatment to the activation step by activation of a reducing agent on the substrate surface for promoting the formation of metallic clusters on the substrate surface during the subsequent activation step, e.g. Sn based solution - Activating in C23C18/28 and lower: Formation of catalytic site on the substrate surface by reduction of metal ions and deposition of metallic clusters, thereby facilitating subsequent electroless plating steps, e.g. Pd, Ag, Au, based solution

[C23C 2/00] Coating by applying the coating material in the molten state -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Metallic coatings obtained by dipping or immersing a substrate into a molten bath of the coating material, where the substrate itself remains essentially unchanged, as well as any methods and/or apparatuses specifically used thereof.  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: Metals and metals alloys, also including inorganic materials such as oxides, carbides, nitrides, borides, silicides and their mixtures

[C23C 2/0034] Details related to elements immersed in bath -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Elements that are immersed within the bath, such as walls, baffles, pumps, elements supporting the substrate during coating or elements for moving the substrate through the bath. Non-moving immersed elements are classified here.
[C23C 2/00342] Moving elements, e.g. pumps or mixers -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Elements that are immersed within the bath which are in motion relative to the bath, such as pumps (i.e. the internal impeller moves relative to the bath), mixers, impellers, rollers or bearings.
[C23C 2/00344] Means for moving substrates, e.g. immersed rollers or immersed bearings -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Elements that are immersed within the bath and act to force movement of the substrate through the bath, such as rollers or portions thereof, e.g. bearings.

[C23C 2/0036] Crucibles -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Crucibles and heating devices. This area also covers the vessel for a holding bath.

[C23C 2/00362] Details related to seals, e.g. magnetic means
[C23C 2/0038] characterised by the pre-treatment chambers located immediately upstream of the bath or occurring locally before the dipping process -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Pre-treatment chamber(s), and elements thereof, that are directly associated with the hot-dipping or immersion apparatus, such as specific structure of pretreatment chamber(s), chamber mechanisms, transportation mechanism, seals, or heat or atmospheric conditions.  **Glossary:** - Locally: The same physical location, e.g. plant, so as to exclude pre-treatment chamber(s) which treat a substrate which then require shipping the pre-treated substrate from one location to another

[C23C 22/00] Chemical surface treatment of metallic material by reaction of the surface with a reactive medium -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Methods, compositions and apparatus for chemical surface treatment of metallic material by reaction of the metallic surface with a reactive liquid to form conversion or passivation coatings thereon.  This group covers also suspensions containing reactive liquids and non-reactive solid particles.  Apparatus for treating metallic material to form conversion coatings thereon ( C23C22/00 ).  General methods or special ones for forming conversion coatings on metallic materials that do not have an appropriate subgroup ( C23C22/00 ).  Conversion coatings ( C23C22/00 - C23C22/47 ).  C23C22/02 . using non-aqueous solutions  C23C22/05 . using aqueous solutions  C23C22/70 . using melts  Passivation, oxidation coatings ( C23C22/48 - C23C22/58 ).  Conversion coatings characterized by the process ( C23C22/73 ).  Pretreatment of the material to be coated ( C23C22/78 ).  After-treatment ( C23C22/82 ).  Regeneration of the coating bath ( C23C22/86 ).  **Glossary:** - Metallic material: covers metals and alloys (attention is drawn to the Note following the title of subclass C22C ). - Phosphate coatings: Phosphate coatings are processes of chemical conversion on a metal surface to produce thin adherent phosphate compound coatings. The phosphate crystals formed on the surfaces of materials can be iron, zinc, or manganese phosphates. Among these phosphates, manganese phosphate is more suitable for wear applications. Phosphate coatings are usually applied to carbon steel, low-alloy steel, and cast iron. They can also be applied to zinc, cadmium, aluminum, and tin. Phosphate processes are hard to apply on high alloys for these alloys are likely immune to the phosphoric acid. In short, phosphating is one of the most useful non-metallic conversion coatings. - Chromate coatings: Chromate coatings, similar to phosphate coatings, are processes of chemical conversion. But the chromate coatings are formed by the reaction of water solutions of chromic acid or chromium salts. The coatings can be applied to aluminum, zinc, cadmium, and magnesium. The coatings usually have good atmospheric corrosion resistance. Chromate coatings are widely used in protecting common household products, such as screws, hinges, and many hardware items with the yellow-brown appearance. - Oxide coatings: The oxide coatings are in fact corrosion products which is a thin, usually less than 2.5 µm oxide with good adhesion. The oxide treatments are done by heat, chemicals, or electrochemical reactions. - Bluing-type oxidations: gun -bluing -type oxidations are done by heating the metals, generally steel, at 370ºC in a steam atmosphere. Chemical baths produce coatings similar to a gun bluing coating by immersion techniques. - Black oxide or blackening coatings: Black oxide or blackening coatings is a conversion coating for steel, copper, zinc, powder metals and silver solder, and most for stainless steel by treating with hot caustic soda (blackening agent). Some pastes can be rubbed on surfaces to produce similar results.

[C23C 2/30] Fluxes or coverings on molten baths -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Fluxes or covering materials for molten baths, e.g. fluxes materials used in hot dipping process  **Limiting references (this place does not cover):** - Removing excess of molten coatings from elongated material by rubbing -> C23C2/22  **Glossary:** - Covering: A chemical compound and/or composition, usually immiscible with the melt and having a lower density, i.e. not a physical object.
[C23C 2/32] using vibratory energy applied to the bath or substrate -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Application of vibrations using physical, magnetic or other means to the bath or to the substrate. An example of subject matter covered by this group is the use of ultrasonic energy to a substrate to cause vibrations of the substrate to enhance wettability of the substrate.
[C23C 2/325] Processes or devices for cleaning the bath -- **Definition:** This place covers:  Processes for cleaning of the bath and the devices that perform the cleaning.  "Cleaning" is intended to cover removal, by chemical or physical means, of impurities within the bath, such as devices which skim material from the surface of the bath or which remove a portion of the bath for treatment to remove impurities before returning the treated portion to the bath.
